## Assistant (2026-04-21 15:10:28)

I’m reconstructing the argument from the transcript and cross-checking it against the current TeX, then I’ll separate what is genuinely proved from what was only asserted so the audit is clean.

I’ve pinned down the current state in the TeX: the draft does **not** claim an unconditional two-point closure anymore; it keeps only the minimal finite-order criterion, the weaker quotient-diagonal route, and the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route. I’m now checking which earlier “closure” claims from the transcript survive the actual formulas and which do not.

_Thought for 5m 31s_

I retraced the two-point/source-level line all the way through. The clean conclusion is:

The **unconditional source-summed two-point closure is not correct**. What *is* correct is a sharper, smaller package:

1. a **formal quadratic divisibility lemma** for any analytic two-atom package with swap symmetry, axis collapse, and diagonal merger;
2. a **real obstruction** showing the naive source-summed corrected-block/whitening route cannot supply the needed linear-in-amplitude one-atom law;
3. a **real quotient-level gain**: the weighted one-atom path is already trivial in the ambient quotient \(\Qabs\) to all orders;
4. a **weaker exact two-atom quotient route** that would exclude exact close bad two-point cores if continuity and diagonal collapse of the actual two-atom quotient germ are proved;
5. and, beyond that, the genuinely live issue is now **purely two-atom**, not one-atom. turn10file1turn12file3turn14file0turn13file2

Here is the rebuilt argument, with the audit.

## 1. The formal lemma is sound

Let \(V\) be any finite-dimensional complex vector space, let \(F_h\in V\), and let
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in V
\]
be analytic near small two-atom data. Assume:

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},\qquad
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1},
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]

Define the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}.
\]

Then
\[
\mathcal I_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0,
\]
so analyticity gives
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2).
\]
Swap symmetry gives \(G(h_1,h_2)=G(h_2,h_1)\). Diagonal merger gives \(G(h,h)=0\). Writing
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad s=h_2-h_1,\qquad \widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right),
\]
the symmetry makes \(\widetilde G\) even in \(s\), and \(\widetilde G(m,0)=0\). Therefore \(\widetilde G(m,s)\) is divisible by \(s^2\), hence
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2
\]
for analytic \(\mathcal J_2\). This part is mathematically correct. It is the right abstract engine behind the two-point theorem. turn10file0

So the real question was never the divisibility argument itself. The real question was whether the **actual corrected two-atom object** satisfies the three hypotheses above.

## 2. The downstream exclusion mechanism is also sound

The conversation correctly reduced the two-point branch to quadratic control of the three finite-order defects:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}.
\]
Once those are \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), the strengthened coincidence theorem forces
\[
\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
while on a compact good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), the map \(h\mapsto v_5(h)/c(h)\) is bi-Lipschitz, so \(|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim |h_1-h_2|\). That contradiction rules out nontrivial close two-point bad cores on such a patch. This reduction was identified early and remains correct. turn10file0

So the entire source-level problem really is: produce the quadratic \((h_1-h_2)^2\) defect factor in a legitimate way.

## 3. The unconditional source-summed theorem is **not** correct

This is the key audit point.

A midpoint proposal in the conversation claimed that one could define a source-summed corrected finite-order package by inserting
\[
q_\mu=\sum_j a_j q_{h_j},\qquad \Phi_\mu=\sum_j a_j\Phi_{h_j}
\]
into the corrected same-point and mixed blocks, then whitening, then extracting cubic/quintic/septic coefficients, and that this would give a source-defined package with
\[
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=aF_h,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)=\mathfrak P_{\le 7}((a_1+a_2)\delta_h).
\]
That claim does **not** survive audit. It is incompatible with the actual amplitude dependence of the corrected blocks. turn10file1turn11file1

The obstruction is explicit. For a weighted one-atom datum
\[
q_{a,h}=a\,q_h,\qquad \Phi_{a,h}=a\,\Phi_h,
\]
the corrected same-point and mixed blocks have the form
\[
G^{\corr}_{a,h,\pm}(s)=a\,\mathcal G_{h,\pm}(a^2;s),
\qquad
N^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)=a\,\mathcal N_h(a^2;s).
\]
After whitening,
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a,h}(s)
=
\mathcal G_{h,-}(a^2;s)^{-1/2}\,
\mathcal N_h(a^2;s)\,
\mathcal G_{h,+}(a^2;s)^{-1/2},
\]
so the overall factor of \(a\) cancels. Therefore every fixed finite-order coefficient extracted from the whitened block is an **even analytic function of \(a\)**. In particular, the naive linear law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a\delta_h)=aF_h
\]
cannot hold on any nonzero patch unless the package vanishes identically. The diagonal additivity
\[
Q_h(a_1+a_2)=Q_h(a_1)+Q_h(a_2)
\]
also fails for a nonzero even analytic function. turn11file1

So the source-summed corrected-block route is not just unproved. In the strong linear form, it is the wrong theorem.

## 4. What *does* survive from the one-atom analysis

The conversation then found the right correction: the weighted one-atom path is not linear in the **raw representative**, but it is trivial in the **ambient quotient**.

At fixed \(h\), varying \(a\neq 0\) changes only the local value data:
\[
(q_h,\Phi_h)\mapsto (a q_h, a\Phi_h).
\]
By the quotient definition used in the draft, \(\Qabs\) is the odd-germ quotient by the value/gauge family. So the weighted one-atom amplitude path lies entirely inside the modded-out family. Hence, on each connected nonzero amplitude interval,
\[
F_{a,h}=F_{a_0,h}\quad\text{in }\Qabs[[z^2]].
\]
That is, the one-atom source-weight path is quotient-trivial to all orders. turn12file4turn14file4

This reconciles the earlier obstruction:

- at the **raw block** level, the representative can vary nontrivially and even in \(a\);
- at the **quotient** level, that variation is invisible, because \(\Qabs\) was defined to kill it. turn14file4

That also means the earlier attempt to make the live target a one-atom septic transport statement was a false fork. The conversation correctly walked that back. The one-atom path is no longer the blocker. turn13file0turn14file2

## 5. There is a real order-\(\le 5\) gain, but it does not finish the theorem

The next useful reduction was this: through order \(\le 5\), the one-atom amplitude path is already invisible in the explicit quotient model. Concretely, for a cubic-normalized weighted one-atom raw germ
\[
R_{a,h}(z)=A_3(h)z^3+A_5(a,h)z^5+O(z^7),
\]
the class \([A_5(a,h)]\) in the first residual quotient is constant in \(a\). Equivalently, the weighted one-atom path contributes no new first residual quotient data, and the genuinely remaining source-level ambiguity starts only at the canonical order-\(7\) level. turn12file1turn12file2

That is a real theorem-level gain. But it still does **not** close the two-point theorem, because the two-point theorem is not ultimately a one-atom transport problem anymore. It is a two-atom interaction problem.

## 6. The direct ambient-quotient two-atom route gives a theorem — and also an obstruction

Once the one-atom path was understood, the next attack defined the genuine two-atom quotient object
\[
F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=[R_{a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2}(z)]\in \Qabs[[z^2]].
\]
At that level, three exact properties are immediate:

\[
F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=F_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1)
\]
(swap symmetry),

\[
F_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=F_{h_1},\qquad F_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=F_{h_2}
\]
(axis collapse),

and
\[
F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h
\]
(diagonal collapse),

because on the axes or diagonal the source reduces to a single weighted atom, and the weighted one-atom class is quotient-trivial. turn14file1

That is a real theorem. But it is **too weak** for the quadratic factorization route. The quotient has erased the amplitude information you would need to build an analytic remainder of the form
\[
F_2=\lambda_1(a_1,a_2,\dots)F_{h_1}+\lambda_2(a_1,a_2,\dots)F_{h_2}+I_2
\]
with \(I_2\) vanishing on axes and diagonal in a way that forces
\[
I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2J_2.
\]
So the ambient-quotient route is exact enough to support a **weaker close-core exclusion**, but too collapsed to give the strong analytic interaction factorization. turn14file3

## 7. The strongest correct rebuilt picture

After auditing everything, the mathematically correct state is:

First, the **strong finite-order source-level route** remains:
construct an actual two-atom finite-order package through orders \(3,5,7\) satisfying

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},\qquad
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1},
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]

If that exists, quadratic divisibility is formal, and the two-point bad-core branch dies on compact good patches. This part is logically sound. It is just not proved for the actual corrected package. turn10file0turn13file2

Second, the **weaker exact quotient-diagonal route** is also sound:
if one can define the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ continuously on normalized two-pair data and prove exact diagonal collapse
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=F_h
\]
on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), then exact close bad two-point cores are excluded by compactness and continuity. This route is weaker than the quadratic-factor route, but coherent. turn14file3

Third, the derivative-geometric fallback on good overlap patches is the \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow route. That route reduces close exact mixed two-point accumulation to the explicit exceptional set
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
with the off-septic-zero part of \(K_v=0\) already absorbed by existing mixed low-order obstructions, and the conditional exact fixed-shear slice \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v\neq 0\}\) transferring into the established nonmixed four-point geometry. So the truly live derivative-geometric residue is concentrated on the \(K_v=0\) lane. turn5file2turn5file3

## 8. Final audit: what is correct, what is not

Correct and verified:

- the formal quadratic divisibility lemma from swap symmetry + axis collapse + diagonal merger; turn10file0
- the downstream reduction from quadratic defect bounds to exclusion on compact good patches; turn10file0
- the even-in-amplitude obstruction for the naive source-summed whitened block; turn11file1
- one-atom amplitude triviality in the ambient quotient \(\Qabs\); turn12file4turn14file4
- order-\(\le 5\) amplitude invisibility in the explicit quotient model; turn12file1
- the weaker exact two-atom quotient-diagonal conditional route; turn14file3
- the three-route final state-of-play. turn13file2

Not correct, and should not be treated as proved:

- the unconditional theorem obtained by source-summing \(q_\mu,\Phi_\mu\), whitening, and claiming
  \[
  \mathfrak P_{\le 7}(a\delta_h)=aF_h
  \]
  or coincident-atom additivity for that raw package; turn11file1
- any claim that the raw source-summed corrected finite-order model alone closes the two-point theorem. turn11file1

Still open:

- an actual **two-atom** amplitude-sensitive package or quotient transport theorem that yields the strong quadratic factorization;
- or, failing that, a proof of continuity plus diagonal collapse for the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ;
- plus the remaining \(K_v=0\) mixed two-point residue. turn14file3turn5file2

So the honest rebuilt mathematical argument is:

the one-atom obstruction has been removed at the quotient level; the naive raw source-summed route is dead; the ambient quotient route is exact but too coarse for the strong factorization; and the true unresolved problem is now a **purely two-atom** interaction theorem. That is the sharpest correct reconstruction of the whole conversation.

_Thought for 1m 43s_

Yes. It **does** sharpen the picture, but in a very specific way.

It does **not** overturn the audit we just made. The strong source-summed closure is still dead, and the real bottleneck is still package-level. What this new note adds is a cleaner **local endgame for the residual mixed corner**: once the \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow analysis has reduced accumulation to
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\]
and then further to the residual corner
\[
S=0,\qquad K_v=0,
\]
the remaining branch is involutive and quotient-diagonal in the local parameter \(t\mapsto -t\). That is a genuine sharpening of the geometry.  

The strongest part of the pasted argument is this reframing:

- the overlap geometry is now fully split into the three explicit lanes
  \((K_v=0,S\neq 0)\), \((S=0,K_v\neq 0)\), and the residual corner \((S=0,K_v=0)\);
- on that residual corner, the exact fixed-shear branch has the involutive local form
  \[
  \Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),\qquad m\ \text{even},\quad G(-t)=G(t),
  \]
  so the bad branch is really a lift of a quotient-diagonal branch, not an arbitrary two-point branch;
- the quotient transport scalar ladder and quartic–sextic rung then show a real local no-reentry phenomenon after quotienting. 

That is all genuinely useful. It makes the mixed residual corner feel much more rigid than before.

Where I would be careful is the proposed “Residual involutive defect criterion.” As written, it is **good but still conditional**. Its logical core is fine:

if along the involutive branch
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),\,E_{12}^{(5)}(t)
\]
are even in \(t\) and vanish at \(t=0\), then they are \(O(t^2)\), hence \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and then the defect-scale closeness mechanism gives a contradiction for a distinct close branch. That implication is correct. 

But there are two important caveats.

First, this theorem does **not** remove the package-level bottleneck; it just localizes it. The note itself says that the real missing input is still diagonal vanishing of the actual corrected finite-order defects at coincidence, and identifies that as the same kind of source-level merger input already isolated earlier. So it is not a new unconditional closure. It is a sharper way of saying: “on the residual mixed corner, it would be enough to prove evenness plus diagonal vanishing of the actual finite-order defects.” 

Second, I do not think the statement is quite finished yet, because it only uses the cubic and quintic defects. The existing two-point exclusion bridge in the draft history was driven by
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\quad E_{12}^{(5)},\quad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
not just the first two. The earlier conditional corollary and the quantitative coincidence step both use the septic quotient defect as part of the control of \(\widehat\Psi\). So unless there is an extra reason on this involutive fixed-shear slice that the septic quotient defect is automatically \(O(t^2)\) or already absorbed, the proposed theorem is missing one rung. 

That is the main substantive thing I would add to the note:
the residual-corner theorem should probably be stated with
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(t),\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}(t)
\]
all even and diagonally vanishing, unless the draft already proves the septic term is redundant on that exact slice.

So my verdict is:

It **does** sharpen the picture, but not by creating a fourth fundamentally new route. It sharpens the **third**, mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route, by turning its last geometric residue into a very small local criterion:

- geometry reduces the problem to the residual involutive corner;
- there, swap-evenness is probably automatic from unordered-pair symmetry;
- the real remaining input is diagonal vanishing of the actual finite-order interaction defects at coincidence;
- and probably the septic quotient defect has to be included explicitly unless you can prove it is automatically controlled on that slice.  

So the best sharpened global picture now looks like this:

There are still three live two-point lanes overall: the strong finite-order merger route, the weaker exact quotient-diagonal route, and the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route. What the new note improves is the **last** of these: inside that lane, the remaining mixed residual corner is no longer a vague geometric frontier, but a local involutive branch where the only real missing input is package-level defect collapse at coincidence. 

My blunt version: this is a **good refinement**, worth capturing in the draft, but it is **not yet a closure theorem**. It mainly tells you exactly where the last mixed two-point residue lives, and that the remaining obstruction is now extremely concentrated.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 15:23:28)

I’m pulling the relevant parts from the transcript and draft side by side so I can separate what is genuinely established, what is only conditionally reduced, and what new structural findings are worth preserving.

_Thought for 3m 59s_

Here is the consolidated mathematical picture I would treat as the real state of play before we do TeX edits.

## 1. The two-point problem has been reduced to a very small front door

The abstract divisibility mechanism is solid. If one has an actual analytic two-atom package \(\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\) with the three identities
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]
\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},\qquad
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=a_1F_{h_1},
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h,
\]
then the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2=\mathfrak P_2-a_1F_{h_1}-a_2F_{h_2}
\]
automatically factors as
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
So the real theorem is not an asymptotic estimate; it is the existence of a genuine finite-order two-atom package with swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger. L132-L181 L236-L258

The downstream bridge is also already in place. Once the finite-order defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
the defect-scale coincidence theorem on good patches finishes the two-point bad-core branch. So the remaining load is entirely in producing the quadratic factorization, not in inventing a new exclusion mechanism. L185-L198

## 2. The strong unconditional source-summed closure attempt is not valid

One important thing we learned, and which should be reflected explicitly in the draft, is that the earlier unconditional source-summed closure was too strong. The old conditional proposition was using two unstated inputs: zero-source normalization and, more importantly, same-support additivity
\[
Q((a_1+a_2)\delta_h)=Q(a_1\delta_h)+Q(a_2\delta_h),
\]
equivalently one-atom linearity in the source weight. Without that, diagonal collapse does not follow. So the draft does not secretly contain a proof of the source-level theorem. L200-L234

More sharply, the naive source-summed corrected-block route is now a genuine no-go. Along a weighted one-atom path, the corrected block structure yields a whitened object whose extracted finite-order coefficients are even analytic functions of the source weight \(a\), not linear in \(a\). That means the raw source-summed corrected package cannot be the object that satisfies the required merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a\delta_h)=aF_h
\]
unless it vanishes identically. This is a real negative result, not just a missing proof. L7595-L7597 L7643-L7678

So one major update beyond the older draft picture is: the “obvious” source-summed whitened lift is dead, and any successful two-point theorem has to use a different package or transport object. L7936-L7939

## 3. There are now three live two-point routes, not one

The two-point side is no longer a single finite-order merger problem. It now has three distinct live conditional routes.

The first is still the strong finite-order merger route: prove that the actual corrected cubic/quintic/septic two-atom package is analytic on small two-atom data and satisfies swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger. That would force the quadratic interaction factorization directly. L7922-L7929

The second is a weaker exact quotient-diagonal route: if one can construct the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse, that would already exclude exact close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of \(\{c\neq 0\}\), even without the full strong factorization theorem. L7930-L7934

The third is the genuinely new mixed derivative-geometric route: on good overlap patches, the mixed bad branch is naturally governed by \(\lambda\)-sheared source transport, not by raw determinant or quotient data alone. This is the big structural addition that is not yet fully absorbed into the current draft narrative. L7595-L7597 L7871-L7914

## 4. The mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route has become highly structured

On an overlap patch, the mixed exact bad branch can be rewritten using
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
A=c-\eta\lambda,\quad
B=v_5-\xi\lambda,\quad
F=u_5-\gamma\lambda,
\]
so that the exact two-point equations become a repeated-source transport system for the \(\lambda\)-sheared source functions. This is the first genuinely shear-sensitive source-level formulation of the mixed branch. L7712-L7763 L7940-L7949

After freezing a \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, the associated projective secant shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
That is already a major simplification of the mixed overlap geometry. L7765-L7820 L31-L47

Even more sharply, in the exact fixed-shear overlap lane the bad set splits into three pieces: if \(S=0\) and \(K_v\neq 0\), the branch transfers to nonmixed four-point geometry; if \(K_v=0\) and \(S\neq 0\), it is already on the mixed low-order obstruction side; and the only genuinely residual mixed corner is
\[
S=0,\qquad K_v=0.
\]
That is one of the main structural findings worth highlighting in the paper. L31-L47

## 5. The residual mixed corner is no longer a vague branch; it is quotient-diagonal and involutive

On the residual exact fixed-shear corner \(K_v=0\), the local projected germ can be written in the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad m\ \text{even},\quad G(-t)=G(t).
\]
So the residual branch satisfies
\[
\Phi(t)=\Phi(-t),
\]
and after passing to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\), it is the pullback of a quotient curve
\[
\Phi(t)=\widehat\Phi(u).
\]
Geometrically, this means the last mixed residue is not a free two-point branch anymore. It is an involutive lift of a quotient-diagonal branch. That is a very strong refinement of the old picture. L49-L71

This connects to the quotient transport scalar
\[
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}
=
2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u).
\]
If
\[
e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D},\qquad r=\ord_0J_\lambda=\ord_0K_v,
\]
then
\[
q-r=2e+2,\qquad m=r+2,\qquad n=r+2e+4,
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
\]
So the residual exact fixed-shear lane lives on an even-support ladder over \(K_v=0\), while the source Wronskian still vanishes to odd order. That is a clean structural theorem in its own right. L73-L117

At the first surviving rung,
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0),
\]
one has
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0,
\]
so \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective in \(u=t^2\). In other words, on the quartic–sextic rung there is no local exact fixed-shear re-entry after quotienting the involution. That is a genuine no-go result, even though it is not by itself the full exclusion theorem. L119-L141

## 6. The best remaining local theorem is now very small

The cleanest proposed endgame on the residual corner is the “residual involutive defect criterion.” Along a local involutive branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\]
if the actual corrected finite-order defects are even in \(t\) and vanish at \(t=0\), then they are automatically \(O(t^2)\), hence \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and then defect-scale closeness forces \(h_1=h_2\), contradicting a distinct two-point branch. So this would exclude the residual exact fixed-shear involutive branch using only objects already defined in the paper. L145-L223

What makes this useful is that it translates the residual mixed corner into a very small package-level task: show swap-evenness and diagonal vanishing of the actual finite-order defects on coincidence. The geometry is no longer the main obstacle there. The remaining issue is the collapse of the corrected package at coincidence. L227-L260

I would, however, record one caution before turning that into TeX: the older two-point reduction used the full trio
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\quad E_{12}^{(5)},\quad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
whereas the proposed residual involutive theorem only names the cubic and quintic defects. So as it stands, I would treat it as nearly right but probably still needing either a septic rung in the statement or a separate reason that the septic quotient defect is redundant on that exact slice. That is an inference from the two reductions, not something I would overstate as already proved. L192-L198 L164-L183

## 7. The most important “goodies”

The biggest structural goodies, to my mind, are these.

First, the overlap bad set is now explicitly split into three lanes, with only one genuine residual corner left:
\[
(K_v=0,\ S\neq 0),\qquad (S=0,\ K_v\neq 0),\qquad (S=0,\ K_v=0).
\]
That is a huge simplification of the mixed side. L31-L47

Second, the residual mixed corner is quotient-diagonal and involutive, not a generic two-point branch. That is the right geometric interpretation of the remaining mixed residue. L49-L71

Third, the even-support residual ladder
\[
q-r=2e+2,\qquad m=r+2,\qquad n=r+2e+4
\]
with odd-order source Wronskian vanishing is a clean structural package that belongs in the architecture remarks. L73-L117

Fourth, the quartic–sextic rung is already quotient-injective, so local re-entry is gone there. That is a good theorem-level no-go to preserve. L119-L141

Fifth, the real bottleneck is now package-level, not geometry-level. The geometry has narrowed the problem down as far as it reasonably can; what remains is collapse of the actual corrected two-atom package at coincidence, either in the strong merger sense or in the weaker defect-vanishing sense. L151-L223

## 8. The key negative findings

The strongest negative finding is that the naive source-summed corrected-block route is blocked by an even-in-amplitude obstruction, so the raw source-summed whitened coefficients cannot be the sought merger object. L7643-L7678

A second negative finding is that determinant-only and quotient-only routes on the mixed side are shear-blind: they do not see the repeated-node shear parameter, so they cannot by themselves close the mixed branch. That is why the \(\lambda\)-shear route is genuinely new rather than just cosmetic reformulation. L7681-L7705

A third negative finding is methodological: the current draft should not be written as if the two-point branch is already closed. The right “front door” statements are still the minimal finite-order source criterion, the weaker quotient-diagonal proposition, and now the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route. L7595-L7597 L7917-L7955

## 9. The shortest honest summary

If I had to compress the full picture into one paragraph, it would be this:

The strong algebraic heart of the two-point theorem is now completely clear: swap symmetry + one-amplitude collapse + diagonal merger give the quadratic \((h_1-h_2)^2\) factor formally, and the downstream defect-scale exclusion is already done. But the naive source-summed corrected-block model cannot furnish that merger law, because its one-atom finite-order outputs are even in the source weight. So the two-point side is still open, but now in a very narrow way: either prove the actual finite-order two-atom merger theorem, or prove the weaker exact quotient-diagonal continuity/collapse theorem, or finish the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route on the residual corner \(S=0=K_v\), where the geometry has already reduced the branch to an involutive quotient-diagonal problem. L132-L181 L7643-L7678 L7871-L7914 L31-L71

That is the version I would now encode into the draft.

## 1) Insert a residual-corner proposition/corollary/remark

Insert this **immediately after** the end of

```latex
\begin{remark}[Quotient-cusp interpretation and the no-reset issue]
\label{rem:quotient-cusp-interpretation-no-reset-Kv-zero}
...
\end{remark}
```

Use:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Residual involutive defect criterion on the exact fixed-shear corner]
\label{prop:residual-involutive-defect-criterion-fixed-shear-corner}
Assume the additional conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane near a residual
accumulation point
\[
a\in \{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}.
\]
Let a local exact repeated-value branch be parametrized by
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad
h(0)=a,
\qquad
h'(0)\neq 0,
\]
with $h$ analytic. Let
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)
\]
denote the cubic and quintic normalized interaction defects along this branch.

Assume:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=E_{12}^{(3)}(-t),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=E_{12}^{(5)}(-t),
\]
and
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(0)=0,
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(0)=0.
\]

Then
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
it follows that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

Consequently no such nontrivial exact residual fixed-shear involutive bad
branch can persist on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By evenness and vanishing at $t=0$, the Taylor expansions have no constant or
odd-order terms:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\alpha_2 t^2+O(t^4),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\beta_2 t^2+O(t^4).
\]
So
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since
\[
h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
we have
\[
t=O(h_1-h_2),
\]
and therefore
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

Now apply Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close} on a
compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
It gives
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C_J\Bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\Bigr)
=
O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
For sufficiently small nonzero $|h_1-h_2|$ this is impossible. Hence no such
nontrivial exact residual fixed-shear involutive bad branch can persist.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Package-level reduction on the residual exact fixed-shear corner]
\label{cor:package-level-reduction-residual-fixed-shear-corner}
In the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:residual-involutive-defect-criterion-fixed-shear-corner},
it is enough to verify for the actual corrected cubic and quintic two-pair
defects that:

\begin{enumerate}
\item they are invariant under swapping the two atoms along the involutive
parametrization $t\leftrightarrow -t$; and

\item they vanish on coincident atoms.
\end{enumerate}

Under these two package-level inputs, the exact residual fixed-shear corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
is excluded on compact good overlap patches.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The two hypotheses are exactly the evenness and diagonal-vanishing inputs of
Proposition~\ref{prop:residual-involutive-defect-criterion-fixed-shear-corner}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The residual exact fixed-shear corner is now a package-level problem]
\label{rem:residual-fixed-shear-corner-now-package-level}
The point of
Proposition~\ref{prop:residual-involutive-defect-criterion-fixed-shear-corner}
is that it does not require construction of the full corrected two-atom quotient
map. Once the residual exact fixed-shear branch is recognized as
quotient-diagonal / involutive, the remaining burden is no longer a new local
mixed branch classification. It is the package-level collapse of the actual
finite-order two-pair defects on coincident atoms, or equivalently a
no-hidden-reset statement for whatever transported overlap state survives on the
quotient side.
\end{remark}
```

This is the cleanest new theorem-strength insertion that is still honest about what remains open. It turns the residual corner into a small package-level criterion rather than another vague geometric frontier.  

## 2) Replace `\label{rem:wip-mixed-lambda-shear-route-status}`

```latex
\begin{remark}[Status of the mixed $\lambda$-shear route]
\label{rem:wip-mixed-lambda-shear-route-status}
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-mixed-lambda-shear-projective-shadow-reduction}

\[
\mathbf\Sigma(h_1,h_2)
=
[x_1S_2-x_2S_1:\ Y_1S_2-Y_2S_1:\ S_2-S_1],
\qquad

\]
independently of any affine freezing of the branch-generated $\lambda$-shears.

Finally,
Proposition~\ref{prop:residual-involutive-defect-criterion-fixed-shear-corner}
shows that on this residual corner it is enough to prove package-level evenness
and diagonal vanishing of the actual cubic/quintic two-pair defects. So the
remaining mixed two-point burden is now best understood as one of three
package-level alternatives: finite-order source-level merger, quotient-diagonal
continuity/diagonal collapse, or a no-hidden-reset theorem for the transported
overlap state on the quotient transport side.
\end{remark}
```

This updates the status remark so it reflects the full split of the overlap bad set and the new residual-corner criterion.

```latex
\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]

Thus the remaining issue beyond the present two-pair subsection is no longer a

the two-point side.

First, the stronger finite-order source-level merger route would force the

patches.

Second, the weaker quotient-diagonal route would already exclude exact close

finite-order defects, or else a no-hidden-reset theorem for the quotient
transport state.

Beyond that lie the genuinely multi-pair interaction bookkeeping through orders

\end{remark}
```

## Assistant (2026-04-21 15:43:34)

I’m checking for places where the draft still speaks as if the two-point story is either broader or more open than it really is, and for any remarks that still point at dead routes.

_Thought for 51s_

Yes. A few things are stale enough that I would actively search for and update or delete them.

The main stale pattern is any wording that still treats the mixed residual frontier as the whole union
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
That was an earlier stopping point. The sharper picture is now: \((K_v=0,S\neq 0)\) is already mixed low-order, \((S=0,K_v\neq 0)\) already transfers to nonmixed \(4\)-point, and the only genuinely residual exact fixed-shear corner is
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}.
\]
So any summary remark that says the remaining mixed two-point issue is “the loci \(\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}\)” is stale and should be narrowed to the residual corner.  

The second stale pattern is any sentence that still says the remaining off-\(K_v=0\) step is a “parity identification” or “matching to the nonmixed odd-zero package.” That has been overtaken by the stronger absorption statement: the slice
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v\neq 0\}
\]
is already transferred into established nonmixed \(4\)-point geometry, not merely “best interpreted” that way. So those softer transition sentences should be removed rather than weakened. 

The third stale pattern is any line suggesting the naive source-summed corrected-block construction is still a plausible closure route. It is not. The even-in-amplitude audit shows that along a weighted one-atom path the extracted finite-order coefficients are even in the source weight, so that model cannot supply the linear merger law. Any summary that still presents that source-summed whitened package as the expected theorem vehicle should be rewritten as a negative finding. 

The fourth stale pattern is any remark that sounds like “the two-point branch is closed” or “the finite-order source-level corrected block theorem now supplies the quadratic factorization.” That was an intermediate overclaim and got superseded by the audit: the strong finite-order merger route is still conditional, the weaker quotient-diagonal exact route is also conditional, and the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear route now concentrates on the residual corner. So any globally triumphant “two-point is done” sentence should be downgraded to the three-route picture.  

The fifth stale pattern is any final-summary wording that says the remaining mixed residue is simply “the \(K_v=0\) lane.” That was already sharper than the full union, but it is still now a bit too coarse. The better statement is: the only genuinely residual **exact fixed-shear** mixed corner is
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
and on that corner the branch is quotient-diagonal / involutive, with the quartic–sextic first rung already locally quotient-injective.  

The sixth stale pattern is any roadmap remark that presents the remaining problem as “more geometry.” The geometry has already done most of its work. What remains is package-level: either exact finite-order merger, or exact quotient-diagonal continuity/collapse, or a no-hidden-reset theorem for the transported overlap state on the residual corner. So anywhere the draft still frames the frontier as a generic local-geometry classification problem should be updated.  

So the short cleanup list is:

- remove or update any summary that leaves the frontier at \(\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}\);
- delete any “off-\(K_v=0\) parity step” language;
- rewrite any positive mention of the naive source-summed whitened package as a viable closure route;
- remove any sentence claiming the two-point branch is already closed;

## Assistant (2026-04-21 15:56:46)

I’m checking the current draft’s own “live routes” language against the newer residual-corner refinements, so I can tell you the real remaining attack rather than the older broader one.

_Thought for 36s_

The attack that remains on \(2\)-point is now quite concentrated.

At the highest level, there are still **three conditional routes**:

the strong finite-order merger route, the weaker exact quotient-diagonal route, and the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear / secant-shadow route. The strong route asks for the actual corrected two-pair **cubic/quintic/septic** package to be analytic on small two-atom data and satisfy swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger. The weaker route asks for a genuine corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse. The mixed route passes through the \(\lambda\)-sheared transport system and the projective secant shadow. 

But the **best next attack** is no longer “do more geometry” in general. It is the **package-level residual-corner attack** on the mixed side.

Why that one first: the mixed overlap geometry has already been cut down to the residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
because \((K_v=0,S\neq 0)\) is already mixed low-order and \((S=0,K_v\neq 0)\) already transfers to nonmixed \(4\)-point. On that residual corner the local branch is involutive / quotient-diagonal,
\[
\Phi(t)=\Phi(-t),
\]
and the quotient transport ladder is already understood, with the quartic–sextic first rung locally quotient-injective. So the geometry has essentially done its job there.  

That is exactly why the proposed **Residual involutive defect criterion** is the right immediate theorem to attack. It reduces the residual corner to two concrete verifications for the **actual corrected two-pair package**:

\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=E_{12}^{(3)}(-t),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=E_{12}^{(5)}(-t),
\]
and
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(0)=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(0)=0.
\]

If you get those, then
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
and the existing defect-scale closeness theorem kills the branch on a compact good patch. The note explicitly identifies **diagonal vanishing** here as the real bottleneck, and ties it back to the diagonal-merger input already isolated by the draft’s minimal source-level criterion.  

So my ranking is:

First, attack the **residual exact fixed-shear corner** by proving package-level **swap-evenness + diagonal vanishing** of the actual corrected defects along the involutive branch. That is the most local, most concrete, and most geometry-exhausted remaining task. 

Second, if that stalls, attack the **strong finite-order merger theorem** directly: prove the actual corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package satisfies the source-level merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]
That is still the cleanest algebraic closure route, but it is broader and heavier than the residual-corner criterion. 

Third, if neither of those moves, attack the **weaker quotient-diagonal route**: construct the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse. That would not give the full quadratic factorization, but it would still exclude exact close two-point bad cores on compact subsets of \(\{c\neq 0\}\). 

My honest tactical view is: the most promising remaining attack is **not** another broad transport computation. It is to prove that, on the residual involutive corner, the actual corrected two-pair defect package is even under \(t\mapsto -t\) and collapses on coincidence. That is where the whole \(2\)-point problem now looks smallest. 

One caution from the current picture: the residual-corner theorem as written in the pasted note only uses the cubic and quintic defects, while the strong source-level route in the draft still tracks the cubic/quintic/**septic** package. My own read is that the next attack should either include the septic quotient rung as well, or explicitly show why it is redundant on that exact fixed-shear slice. That is an inference from putting the two formulations side by side, not a theorem already written in the draft.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 15:58:44)

I’m checking the draft-side criterion and the pasted residual-corner theorem together, because the real question is whether the septic quotient rung is genuinely unnecessary on that slice or just got dropped by convenience.

_Thought for 53s_

Yes — I think that caution is real, and the safest refinement is:

**as things stand, the residual-corner theorem should be upgraded to include the septic quotient defect as well.**

The reason is straightforward. The draft-side two-point closure that we actually trust is the strengthened coincidence / defect-scale route, and in that route the controlling package is explicitly
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}.
\]
The earlier reconstruction of the source-level route also treated the two-point problem as closed only once all three are \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\). So the pasted residual theorem, which only assumes evenness and diagonal vanishing for the cubic and quintic defects, is presently **weaker than the closure mechanism it invokes**.  

That means there are really two honest options.

The first, and in my view the right one for the draft right now, is to **state the residual involutive criterion with the full order-\(\le 7\) package**:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(t),\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}(t)
\]
should all be even under \(t\mapsto -t\) and all vanish at \(t=0\). Then the same argument goes through verbatim:
evenness plus vanishing gives each one \(O(t^2)\), hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
=
O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
and now this matches the known two-point closure package exactly. That version is clean and aligned with the current draft architecture.  

The second option would be to prove a **new redundancy lemma** on the exact fixed-shear residual corner saying, in effect, that the septic quotient rung is automatically controlled once the cubic and quintic defects are. But that is not yet in hand. The pasted note itself identifies diagonal vanishing only for the cubic and quintic defects as the bottleneck, but that is because it is aiming at a smaller local criterion, not because the septic quotient rung has been shown redundant. I do not see a theorem in the current picture that justifies dropping \(\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\).  

So I would sharpen the picture this way:

The **residual-corner theorem in its current form is best viewed as a prototype**, not yet the final statement. Its real value is geometric: it shows that on the involutive residual corner the local endgame is package-level and not a new geometry problem. But to plug directly into the existing two-point closure mechanism, it should be rewritten with the full finite-order defect triple through order \(7\).  

Concretely, the refined theorem should look like this:

Assume along the involutive exact fixed-shear branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t))
\]
that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(t),\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}(t)
\]
are even in \(t\), and that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(0)=E_{12}^{(5)}(0)=\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}(0)=0.
\]
Then all three are \(O(t^2)\), hence \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and the existing strengthened coincidence / defect-scale machinery excludes the branch on a compact good patch.

That is the version I would draft into the paper unless we first prove a separate lemma that the septic quotient defect is automatically redundant on that slice.

So my bottom line is: **your caution is correct, and the next refinement should be to restore the septic quotient rung explicitly.** The “cubic + quintic only” version is suggestive, but not yet logically matched to the route the draft actually uses.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:00:56)

I’m checking whether the septic quotient rung can actually be derived from the cubic/quintic data on the involutive residual corner, or whether it really has to be kept in the theorem. If there is a redundancy, it has to come from the quotient structure itself, not just wishful simplification.

_Thought for 1m 11s_

Yes — here is the clean attack, and I think it settles the refinement in the right way.

The right conclusion is:

**the residual-corner theorem should be upgraded to the full**
\[
\bigl(E_{12}^{(3)},\,E_{12}^{(5)},\,\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr)
\]
**package.**

I do **not** see a valid argument, from the current draft picture, that the septic quotient rung is automatically redundant on the residual exact fixed-shear slice. The existing closure mechanism for two-point still runs through the strengthened coincidence bridge, and that bridge was isolated using the full cubic/quintic/septic package. So the cubic+quintic-only residual theorem is presently a prototype, not the logically final statement.  

Here is the sharpened theorem.

Let
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad
h(0)=a,\qquad h'(0)\neq 0,
\]
be a local exact repeated-value branch on the residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
a\in \{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}.
\]
Assume that along this branch
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(t),\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}(t)
\]
are all even in \(t\), and that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(0)=E_{12}^{(5)}(0)=\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}(0)=0.
\]
Then each of them is \(O(t^2)\). Since
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
it follows that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
=
O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
And that is now exactly the finite-order defect package that the trusted two-point closure route wants. So the defect-scale closeness theorem closes the branch on a compact good patch. 

The proof is the same Taylor-parity argument as before, just done for all three defects. If \(F(t)\) is any of the three and
\[
F(t)=F(-t),\qquad F(0)=0,
\]
then
\[
F(t)=\alpha_2 t^2+O(t^4),
\]
hence \(F(t)=O(t^2)\), hence \(F=O((h_1-h_2)^2)\). So the upgraded residual theorem is immediate once the septic rung is included. There is no new analytic difficulty in the proof itself. The real issue is only whether the hypotheses are justified for the actual corrected package.

Now for the real attack: can \(\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\) be dropped?

My read is no, not from anything currently on the table.

The reason is that the residual-corner geometry — parity reduction, quotient-diagonal involution, quotient transport ladder, quartic–sextic injectivity — lives on the **transport scalar / quotient-curve** side. It tells you that the residual branch is highly rigid and that re-entry is hard. But it does **not** give a theorem of the form
\[
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=\mathcal L\!\bigl(E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}\bigr)
\]
or
\[
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=0
\quad\text{whenever}\quad
E_{12}^{(3)}=E_{12}^{(5)}=0
\]
on that slice. Nothing in the current residual-ladder picture produces such a dependence. The quartic–sextic no-reentry statement is about local injectivity of \(\widehat Q(u)\), not about elimination of the septic quotient class in the corrected two-pair defect package. So it is not enough to remove \(\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\).  

So the honest upgrade is:

- **swap-evenness** is plausibly automatic for all three defects, including the septic quotient class, because \(t\mapsto -t\) swaps the two atoms and the corrected two-pair core is an unordered pair;
- **diagonal vanishing** is the real bottleneck, and now it must be asked for at all three levels:
  \[
  E_{12}^{(3)}(0)=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(0)=0,\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}(0)=0.
  \]

That last condition is exactly the order-\(7\) analogue of coincident-atom merger in the quotient-fixed-sector package. It is not a new conceptual problem; it is the same package-level collapse issue, just at the septic quotient rung. 

So the best remaining attack is now even sharper than before:

1. Prove that on the involutive residual fixed-shear branch, the full finite-order defect triple
   \[
   \bigl(E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)},\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr)
   \]
   is even under \(t\mapsto -t\).

2. Prove diagonal vanishing at coincidence for the same triple.

3. Then the upgraded residual-corner theorem is immediate and plugs directly into the existing closure mechanism.

That is the clean attack.

The negative finding that comes with it is also useful: **unless you can prove a separate septic-redundancy lemma, the cubic+quintic-only residual theorem is not enough for the current draft’s trusted closure route.** So I would stop trying to finesse the septic rung away and instead absorb it into the theorem statement now. 

If you want, next I’ll write the exact upgraded theorem in draft-ready LaTeX with the full \(3/5/7\) package.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:03:14)

I’m pushing on the actual mathematical bottleneck now: whether the septic quotient rung can be forced from the same involutive-corner symmetry/diagonal-collapse mechanism, or whether the right theorem is simply the full \(3/5/7\) package.

_Thought for 2m 36s_

Yes — and I think the attack sharpens one step further.

It is not just that the residual-corner theorem should include the septic quotient rung. It should also be stated at the level of the **raw interaction defects**, not the ordered normalized ones.

The reason is that the involution \(t\mapsto -t\) swaps the two atoms. Swap-evenness is therefore naturally a statement about the **unordered two-pair interaction package**. That is exactly where the corrected cubic/quintic/septic defects live before any ordered normalization. By contrast, once you divide by \(a_1\) or otherwise normalize relative to the “first” atom, you break the obvious swap symmetry. So the right parity statement is not
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=E_{12}^{(3)}(-t),
\]
for the ordered normalized defect, but rather
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(t)=\mathcal E^{(3)}(-t),
\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}(t)=\mathcal E^{(5)}(-t),
\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(t)=\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(-t),
\]
for the **raw** cubic, quintic, and septic quotient interaction defects along the involutive branch. That is the natural symmetric object. The draft’s trusted two-point closure mechanism is already framed in terms of the full \(3/5/7\) package, so this is the right level to work on.  

So the genuinely improved residual theorem should be:

Let
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad h(0)=a,\qquad h'(0)\neq 0,
\]
be a local exact repeated-value branch on the residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
a\in \{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}.
\]
Let
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(t),\qquad \mathcal E^{(5)}(t),\qquad \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(t)
\]
denote the raw cubic, quintic, and septic quotient interaction defects of the actual corrected two-pair package along this branch.

Assume:
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(t)=\mathcal E^{(3)}(-t),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}(t)=\mathcal E^{(5)}(-t),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(t)=\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(-t),
\]
and
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(0)=\mathcal E^{(5)}(0)=\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(0)=0.
\]

Then each is \(O(t^2)\), hence, since
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
one gets
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)},\qquad \mathcal E^{(5)},\qquad \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}
=
O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
If the normalized amplitudes stay in a compact set and the normalized defects are obtained from the raw ones by dividing by the usual bounded amplitude factor, then
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
=
O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
which is exactly the package needed by the existing strengthened coincidence / defect-scale-close machinery. So the residual branch is excluded on a compact good patch. 

This is a better theorem than the previous cubic+quintic version for two reasons.

First, it now matches the actual two-point closure package already isolated earlier:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)},\ \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}.
\]
So there is no logical mismatch anymore. 

Second, it puts the parity statement in the right place. Swap-evenness is not something I would want to prove for the ordered normalized defects; that is awkward and possibly false without extra bookkeeping. But for the raw interaction package it is the expected symmetry, because \(t\mapsto -t\) simply swaps the two atoms of the same unordered core. That means the real bottleneck gets even cleaner:

the only substantial remaining input is **diagonal vanishing of the raw \(3/5/7\) interaction package at coincidence**.  

So the attack now looks like this.

The geometry has already reduced the mixed overlap problem to the residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
and there the branch is quotient-diagonal / involutive, with the quotient transport scalar ladder and quartic–sextic no-reentry already in place. That part is no longer the frontier.  

The raw defect triple should be automatically even once the corrected two-pair interaction package is genuinely defined on unordered pairs. So the remaining hard point is not parity. It is coincidence collapse:
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(0)=0,\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}(0)=0,\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(0)=0.
\]

That is exactly the order-\(\le 7\) analogue of diagonal merger, now expressed in the language of raw finite-order defects rather than a full source-level map. It is also why I do not think there is a hidden septic-redundancy miracle here: nothing in the current quotient-transport ladder forces the septic quotient class from the lower-order defects alone. The ladder controls the geometry of the residual branch; it does not collapse the order-\(7\) quotient class automatically. So the septic rung stays. 

So the continuation of the attack is:

prove the **raw** \(3/5/7\) interaction package is swap-symmetric and vanishes on coincident atoms. Once that is in hand, the residual exact fixed-shear corner is gone.

That is materially sharper than where we were one turn ago, because it tells us the right theorem is not “normalized cubic/quintic evenness,” but “raw cubic/quintic/septic quotient collapse on the involutive residual corner.”

This matches the stronger finite-order route already isolated in the draft, which still runs through the cubic/quintic/septic package, while the mixed route has already reduced geometry to the residual corner \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\).   

Here is the sharpened attack.

Let
\[
\mathfrak R_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)

denote the **actual corrected two-pair odd germ class through order \(7\)**, before ordered normalization, and let
\[

\mathcal I^{\rm raw}_{\le 7}(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=

viewed in the order-\(\le 7\) residual quotient that feeds the cubic, quintic fixed-sector, and septic quotient projections. Then define

That is the right package because the trusted two-point closure route still asks for the whole triple
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}
\]
to be \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and the earlier source-level reduction also tracks the cubic/quintic/septic package, not just \(3/5\). So the septic rung is not decorative; it is part of the actual closure input.  

Now suppose we are on the residual exact fixed-shear involutive branch. The geometry already gives that, after local parametrization, the branch is quotient-diagonal / involutive:
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad
\Phi(t)=\Phi(-t),
\]
and the residual local type is organized by the even-support ladder over \(K_v=0\), with the quartic–sextic first rung already locally quotient-injective. So the geometry is no longer the frontier here.  

The new point is this:

## 1. Swap-evenness is not really the bottleneck anymore

For the **raw** interaction package, evenness should be automatic once the corrected two-pair core is genuinely defined on an **unordered** two-atom datum.

Indeed, if the branch is parametrized so that
\[
(a_1(-t),h_1(-t);a_2(-t),h_2(-t))
=
(a_2(t),h_2(t);a_1(t),h_1(t)),
\]
then symmetry of the unordered raw package gives
\[
\mathcal I^{\rm raw}_{\le7}(-t)=\mathcal I^{\rm raw}_{\le7}(t),
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(-t)=\mathcal E^{(3)}(t),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}(-t)=\mathcal E^{(5)}(t),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(-t)=\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(t).
\]

So I would now stop treating parity as a substantive separate theorem. It is a formal consequence of “raw package on unordered pairs.” The real issue is diagonal collapse. This fits the broader reframing that the remaining burden is package-level, not geometry-level.  

## 2. The real remaining theorem is diagonal collapse through order \(7\)

What we actually need is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathfrak R_1(a_1+a_2,h)
\quad\text{through order }7
}
\]
in the residual quotient that feeds the \(3/5/7\) projections.

This is the exact order-\(\le7\) diagonal-merger statement. It is weaker than the full all-orders quotient-diagonal route, because it only asks for equality through the finite package already used downstream. And it is also more precise than the old source-linear theorem, because it is phrased directly at the raw corrected class level.

Why this is enough is immediate. On the diagonal,
\[
\mathcal I^{\rm raw}_{\le 7}(a_1,h;a_2,h)
=
\mathfrak R_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)-\mathfrak R_1(a_1,h)-\mathfrak R_1(a_2,h).
\]
If the diagonal collapse statement holds and the one-pair weighted class is additive on the diagonal in the finite quotient through order \(7\),
\[
\mathfrak R_1(a_1+a_2,h)=\mathfrak R_1(a_1,h)+\mathfrak R_1(a_2,h),
\]
then
\[
\mathcal I^{\rm raw}_{\le 7}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0,
\]
hence
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(0)=\mathcal E^{(5)}(0)=\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(0)=0.
\]

Combined with automatic evenness, this gives
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}(t),\ \mathcal E^{(5)}(t),\ \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since on the involutive branch
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
we get
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)},\ \mathcal E^{(5)},\ \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}
=
O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
After dividing by the bounded normalization factor on normalized families, this is exactly the defect package the established strengthened coincidence / defect-scale-close mechanism uses. So the residual branch is excluded. That is the same defect-scale logic already used in the earlier source-level closure route; the only change is that we are now feeding it with the **raw \(3/5/7\) interaction package on the involutive corner**.  

## 3. Why the septic rung still stays

This attack also clarifies why there is no obvious septic-redundancy miracle.

The quotient transport ladder on the residual corner controls the local geometry of the involutive branch:
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),\qquad
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
with even-support ladder
\[
q-r=2e+2,\qquad m=r+2,\qquad n=r+2e+4,
\]
and quartic–sextic local quotient injectivity on the first rung. But none of that yields a relation of the form
\[
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=\mathcal L(\mathcal E^{(3)},\mathcal E^{(5)})
\]
on the actual corrected two-pair package. Those are different layers: one is transport geometry, the other is the finite corrected interaction package. So unless a new explicit projection identity is proved, the septic quotient class remains an independent rung in the theorem.  

## 4. The minimal live theorem is now very small

So the attack has collapsed to this:

**Minimal residual-corner closure theorem.**  
If the actual corrected two-pair raw class through order \(7\)

1. is symmetric under swapping the two atoms, and  
2. collapses on coincident atoms to the one-pair weighted class through order \(7\),

then on the involutive residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)},\qquad \mathcal E^{(5)},\qquad \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}
\]
are even and vanish at \(t=0\), hence are \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and the branch is excluded on compact good patches.

That is materially sharper than what we had before, because it tells us the real missing theorem is not “some evenness statement,” and not “more transport geometry,” but a **finite order-\(\le7\) diagonal collapse theorem for the raw corrected two-pair class**.

So the next attack I would actually pursue is:

- formalize the raw order-\(\le7\) corrected two-pair class as an unordered object;
- prove swap symmetry at that raw level;
- and then attack the diagonal identity
  \[
  \mathfrak R_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathfrak R_1(a_1+a_2,h)
  \quad\text{through order }7.
  \]

That is now the smallest honest theorem still standing between the residual-corner geometry and a full two-point exclusion.

## What is still hard, and what is no longer hard

Swap-evenness is not the interesting part anymore. On the involutive branch, \(t\mapsto -t\) just swaps the two atoms of the same unordered two-point core, so evenness is the expected formal symmetry of the raw package. The pasted theorem already identifies this as the natural first verification. 

The real bottleneck is diagonal vanishing:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(0)=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(0)=0.
\]
That is exactly the package-level collapse statement the note identifies, and it is the residual-corner version of the draft’s finite-order diagonal-merger criterion. 

So the honest updated attack is:

1. Treat the residual exact fixed-shear theorem as a **cubic/quintic theorem**, not a \(3/5/7\) theorem.
2. Prove those two defects are even under the involution.
3. Prove those two defects vanish on coincident atoms.
4. Then the existing good-patch closeness corollary kills the residual branch.

## What remains true about the septic rung

The septic quotient defect is still important elsewhere.

It remains part of the **stronger finite-order source-level merger route**, because that route is explicitly framed as a cubic/quintic/septic package and its conditional corollary produces the full quadratic defect estimates through order \(7\). turn44file3

So the correct split is:

- **Residual exact fixed-shear corner:** cubic + quintic are enough.
- **Strong general two-point factorization route:** keep cubic + quintic + septic.

That is the main refinement from this attack.

I have not turned that into a clean theorem from the draft text yet, so I would not promote it beyond “possible next refinement” at this stage.

So the best remaining attack on \(2\)-point is now:

**prove diagonal vanishing of the cubic and quintic interaction defects on coincident atoms along the involutive residual exact fixed-shear corner.**

That is smaller than the full source-level merger theorem, smaller than the full quotient-diagonal route, and now looks like the most local live theorem left.

Yes — and pushing on the septic quotient defect actually becomes cleaner once you phrase it at the **right level**.

The key observation is: elsewhere in the two-point story, the septic rung is not the full septic coefficient. What the draft’s strong route actually tracks is the **septic quotient class**
\[
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
or equivalently the third component of the finite-order package valued in
\[
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \bigl(\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\bigr).
\]
So the septic task is already weaker than proving literal order-\(7\) equality of representatives. 

That gives a sharper target:

## The real septic theorem to attack

For the strong finite-order merger route, you do **not** need to prove
\[
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)
\]
as actual vectors in \(\mathfrak f\).

It is enough to prove the weaker **quotient-diagonal collapse**
\[
\boxed{
\bigl[A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)\bigr]
=
\bigl[A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)\bigr]
\quad\text{in }\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)
\in
\mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

That is the right “septic merger” statement. It is materially weaker than full order-\(7\) collapse, and it matches the package the draft actually uses in the conditional strong source-level route. 

So the septic attack is narrower than it looked.

## Why this is the right refinement

The earlier strong finite-order criterion was already reformulated in terms of the package
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus
\bigl(\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\bigr),
\]
with
\[
F_h=
\bigl(c(h),A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),[A_7^{\mathfrak f}](h)\bigr).
\]
So at order \(7\), the theorem is only asking for equality **modulo the quintic line**. 

That means the real diagonal septic input is:

\[
\boxed{
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0,
}
\]
not full equality of raw septic representatives. This is the exact order-\(7\) analogue of diagonal merger at the quotient-fixed-sector level. turn46file4

## The strongest honest attack on the septic rung

So the attack I would now pursue is:

First, keep the cubic and quintic merger statements exactly as before. Those are honest equalities in their natural spaces.

Second, replace the old informal “prove septic collapse” language by the more precise quotient theorem:

> On coincident atoms, the order-\(7\) mismatch of the actual corrected two-pair finite-order package lies in the one-dimensional gauge line \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)\).

Written explicitly, the theorem to prove is:
\[
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)
-
A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

If you get that, then the septic quotient defect vanishes on the diagonal, which is exactly what the strong source-level route needs. 

## Why this is plausible

There is a structural reason this is the right guess.

At order \(7\), the draft is already quotienting by the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line. That strongly suggests the only truly meaningful order-\(7\) obstruction, after cubic/quintic normalization, is the component transverse to that line. So on coincident atoms, once the lower-order data have merged, the remaining order-\(7\) discrepancy is very plausibly a **pure gauge drift along the quintic direction**, not a transverse quotient obstruction. That is exactly the content of
\[
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)
\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

I want to be careful: this is a **plausible target theorem**, not something the draft has already proved. But it is the right sharpening of the septic problem. turn46file4

## What this does to the current route split

This also clarifies the role of the septic rung in the three remaining two-point routes.

For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, the prototype local exclusion theorem really only needs the cubic and quintic defects, because the already-proved good-patch closeness corollary is invoked in the form
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C_J\bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\bigr),
\]
so the septic quotient defect does not enter that local contradiction. turn46file8

But for the **stronger finite-order source-level merger route**, the septic quotient defect still matters, because that route is explicitly organized around the cubic/quintic/septic quotient package through order \(7\). So the septic attack remains load-bearing there. turn46file4

## The negative finding that matters here

There is also an important no-go to keep in mind while pushing on septic:

the draft already audited that determinant-only and quotient-only routes are **shear-blind** on the mixed branch. In particular, “the septic quotient class by itself” does not see the repeated-node shear parameter; it carries no more source-coupled information than the determinant scalar already visible to the quotient side. So the septic rung is important for the strong global source-level package, but it is **not** the right standalone tool for closing the mixed residual corner. 

That is why the right septic attack is diagonal quotient-collapse in the source package, not another attempt to use the septic quotient class as an independent mixed-geometry detector.

## The minimal septic proposition I would now try to prove

If I had to compress the remaining septic burden into one proposition, it would be:

> **Conditional septic quotient diagonal collapse.**  
> Assume the actual corrected two-pair finite-order package through order \(7\) is defined on small two-atom data. Then on coincident atoms,
> \[
> A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)
> \in
> \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
> \]
> Equivalently,
> \[
> \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
> \]

This is exactly the septic piece still needed by the strong source-level merger route, and it is the weakest honest order-\(7\) statement compatible with the package the draft already uses. 

So the next attack I’d recommend is: stop aiming for full order-\(7\) equality, and attack **quotient-diagonal collapse modulo \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)** instead. That is the real septic theorem still standing.

_Thought for 1m 52s_

I think the septic attack now reduces to one very specific mechanism, and it is much cleaner than “prove full order-7 equality.”

The right target is still
\[
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0,
\]
equivalently
\[
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]
because the strong two-point route only tracks the order-7 class in
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
not literal equality of septic representatives. That is exactly the package the conditional finite-order criterion was built around.  

Here is the attack.

## 1. Why quotienting by \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is the right order-7 gauge

At the level of odd expansions, the order-7 ambiguity produced by a residual odd reparametrization is exactly of the form “multiple of the order-5 term.”

Take a model odd expansion
\[
\Gamma(s)=c\,s^3+A_5^{\mathfrak f}s^5+A_7^{\mathfrak f}s^7+O(s^9),
\]
where \(c\) is the cubic scalar channel and \(A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_7^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathfrak f\) are the fixed-sector coefficients. Now apply an odd reparametrization
\[
s=\sigma+\alpha \sigma^3+\beta \sigma^5+O(\sigma^7).
\]
Then
\[
s^3=\sigma^3+3\alpha \sigma^5+(3\beta+3\alpha^2)\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\]
\[
s^5=\sigma^5+5\alpha \sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\qquad
s^7=\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9).
\]
So after substitution, the order-7 coefficient changes by
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\longmapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+5\alpha A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
up to the cubic-generated terms, which live in the lower scalar/gauge sector already handled separately. In other words, once the lower-order normalization is fixed, the **residual order-7 fixed-sector gauge freedom is exactly the line**
\[
\mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

That is the conceptual reason the theorem only asks for equality in
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
and not in \(\mathfrak f\) itself. It is not a hack; it is the natural order-7 gauge quotient.

## 2. What this suggests on coincident atoms

Now specialize to coincident atoms:
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h,h).
\]
There are then two order-\(\le 7\) corrected objects in play:

the coincident two-pair corrected class
\[
\Gamma_{2,h}(s)
\]
coming from the actual corrected two-pair construction with amplitudes \(a_1,a_2\), and the one-pair total-amplitude corrected class
\[
\Gamma_{1,h}^{\mathrm{tot}}(s)
\]
coming from amplitude \(a_1+a_2\).

The cubic/quintic merger route is asking for these to agree through order \(5\). Once that lower-order identification is in place, the only plausible remaining discrepancy at order \(7\) is a residual odd reparametrization of the common local parameter. And as above, such a reparametrization moves the fixed-sector septic term only by
\[
\mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

So the septic theorem we want is precisely:

> **Coincident-atom septic quotient collapse.**  
> After identifying the coincident two-pair corrected class and the one-pair total-amplitude corrected class through cubic and quintic order, their order-7 fixed-sector mismatch is purely gauge:
> \[
> A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
> \]

Equivalently,
\[
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]

That is the weakest honest septic theorem, and it is exactly what the strong finite-order route needs. 

## 3. What has actually been reduced, and what is still missing

I do **not** think this is a full proof yet. But it reduces the septic burden to one very explicit lemma:

> **Frame-gauge lemma at coincidence.**  
> On coincident atoms, once the cubic scalar and quintic fixed-sector data have merged, the actual corrected two-pair order-\(\le 7\) class and the one-pair total-amplitude order-\(\le 7\) class differ only by an odd reparametrization of the local parameter.

If that lemma is true, the septic quotient collapse is immediate from the substitution calculation above.

So the attack has reduced the septic problem from “prove some mysterious order-7 identity” to:

1. prove the two coincident constructions are related by a common odd local reparametrization after lower-order identification;
2. then the quotient by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) kills the remaining order-7 ambiguity automatically.

That is a real reduction.

## 4. Why this does not help the residual-corner theorem directly

This also explains the split between the two live routes.

For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, the local exclusion theorem on a compact good patch only needs the cubic and quintic defects, via
\[
|h_1-h_2|\le C_J\bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\bigr).
\]
So the septic quotient collapse is not needed there. 

But for the **stronger source-level merger route**, the septic quotient class remains part of the finite-order package, so this quotient-diagonal collapse modulo \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is still load-bearing. 

## 5. The most honest current theorem statement

So the best current statement I think we can defend is:

> If the actual corrected two-pair and one-pair total-amplitude constructions on coincident atoms agree through cubic and quintic order in a common normalized frame, then their order-7 fixed-sector mismatch lies in the gauge line \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)\). Hence the septic quotient defect vanishes on the diagonal:
> \[
> \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
> \]

That is not yet a completed proof, but it is a much sharper attack than before, and I think it isolates the real missing septic lemma correctly.

The practical next step is to make that frame-gauge lemma explicit and attack it, rather than continuing to treat the septic rung as if it required full order-7 equality.
