_Thought for 1m 51s_

I attacked it, and I think the septic problem really does collapse to a much smaller lemma.

The strong two-point route is only asking for the order-\(7\) class in
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
not literal equality of septic representatives. That is already built into the package the draft tracks:
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\in
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus
\bigl(\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\bigr),
\]
and the corresponding defect is \(\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\), not a raw \(A_7\)-difference in \(\mathfrak f\). 

So the order-\(7\) target is:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)
\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0
\]
on coincident atoms. That is the weakest honest septic theorem still needed by the strong finite-order merger route. 

The main calculation is this. Write a common odd expansion in a local parameter \(s\):
\[
\Gamma(s)=c\,s^3+A_5^{\mathfrak f}s^5+A_7^{\mathfrak f}s^7+O(s^9).
\]
Now apply an odd reparametrization
\[
s=\sigma+\alpha \sigma^3+\beta \sigma^5+O(\sigma^7).
\]
Then
\[
s^3=\sigma^3+3\alpha \sigma^5+(3\beta+3\alpha^2)\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\]
\[
s^5=\sigma^5+5\alpha \sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\qquad
s^7=\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9).
\]
So
\[
\Gamma(s(\sigma))
=
c\,\sigma^3
+
\bigl(A_5^{\mathfrak f}+3\alpha c\bigr)\sigma^5
+
\bigl(A_7^{\mathfrak f}+5\alpha A_5^{\mathfrak f}+(3\beta+3\alpha^2)c\bigr)\sigma^7
+
O(\sigma^9).
\]

After projecting away the lower scalar/value channel, the only order-\(7\) fixed-sector change caused by reparametrization is
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\longmapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+5\alpha A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
So the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
is invariant under the residual odd reparametrization freedom once cubic and quintic normalization have been fixed. That is the structural reason the septic quotient is the right object. It is not cosmetic; it is exactly the order-\(7\) gauge-invariant remainder. 

That means the septic burden reduces to a single frame-comparison lemma.

Let \(\Gamma_{2,h}\) be the corrected coincident two-pair germ for \((a_1,h;a_2,h)\), and let \(\Gamma_{1,h}^{\mathrm{tot}}\) be the corrected one-pair germ with total amplitude \(a_1+a_2\). If, after choosing lower-order normalized coordinates, these two germs agree through cubic and quintic order, then their septic fixed-sector mismatch is automatically pure gauge:
\[
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]
hence
\[
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]

So the septic attack is no longer “do a new order-\(7\) computation.” It is:

prove that, on coincident atoms, the corrected two-pair construction and the corrected one-pair total-amplitude construction are related by a common odd local reparametrization after lower-order matching.

That is the real missing lemma.

I do not think this is a full proof yet. The open point is exactly that last frame-gauge statement: why the coincident two-pair and total-amplitude one-pair germs must differ only by odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower scalar/value gauge. The current draft material does not yet prove that directly. But the order-\(7\) part is now sharply reduced: once that frame-gauge lemma is established, the septic quotient defect vanishes on the diagonal automatically. 

This also clarifies the split between the two surviving two-point lanes.

For the strong finite-order source-level route, you still need the septic quotient rung because that route explicitly controls
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\qquad E_{12}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}.
\]
That is the package fed into the finite-order merger criterion. 

By contrast, for the local residual exact fixed-shear corner, the good-patch closeness corollary is used in the form
\[
|h_1-h_2|\le C_J\Bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\Bigr),
\]
so cubic and quintic are enough there; the septic quotient defect is not part of that local contradiction. 

So the honest outcome of this attack is:

the septic problem has been reduced from “prove full order-\(7\) coincidence” to “prove the coincident two-pair and total-amplitude one-pair germs differ only by lower-order gauge plus odd reparametrization.” If that frame-gauge lemma is true, the quotient-diagonal septic collapse follows immediately.

\[

\]
not literal equality of septic representatives, while the residual-corner route uses only the cubic and quintic defects through the good-patch closeness corollary. Those are genuinely different mechanisms.   

Here is the reduction.

Let the coincident two-pair corrected germ and the total-amplitude one-pair corrected germ be written, in some local odd parameter, as
\[
\Gamma_2(s)=c\,s^3+U\,s^5+V\,s^7+O(s^9),
\qquad
\Gamma_1(\sigma)=c\,\sigma^3+U\,\sigma^5+W\,\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\]
where \(c\) is the cubic scalar channel and \(U=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)\) is the common quintic fixed-sector coefficient after lower-order merger.

Now suppose these two germs differ only by an odd reparametrization
\[
s=\sigma+\alpha \sigma^3+\beta \sigma^5+O(\sigma^7)
\]
together with the lower scalar/value gauge that is already modded out in the draft’s finite-order package.

A direct substitution gives
\[
s^3=\sigma^3+3\alpha \sigma^5+(3\beta+3\alpha^2)\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\]
\[

\qquad
s^7=\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9).
\]
So the order-\(7\) fixed-sector term changes by
\[
V \longmapsto V+5\alpha U
\]
up to the lower scalar channel. Therefore the quotient class
\[
[V]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C U
\]
is invariant under precisely that residual odd reparametrization freedom.

That means: once cubic and quintic merger are known, **any** remaining order-\(7\) discrepancy coming only from odd reparametrization is automatically killed in
\[
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

So the septic quotient collapse
\[
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0
\]
follows from a much smaller lemma:

> **Coincident-frame comparability lemma.**  
> After cubic/quintic lower-order merger on coincident atoms, the actual corrected two-pair germ and the actual corrected one-pair total-amplitude germ differ only by odd local reparametrization plus the lower scalar/value gauge already quotiented out.

If that lemma holds, then the septic quotient defect vanishes on the diagonal automatically. In other words, for the strong source-level route the true missing package is not
\[
(c,\ A_5^{\mathfrak f},\ [A_7^{\mathfrak f}])
\]
with three logically separate diagonal identities; it reduces to:

1. cubic merger,  
2. quintic merger,  
3. coincident-frame comparability.

Then the order-\(7\) quotient identity is formal. This is a real reduction of the strong route. 

So my current view is:

For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, keep attacking cubic and quintic diagonal vanishing, because that route only needs those two defects. 

For the **strong finite-order source-level route**, stop trying to prove a standalone septic diagonal identity. The right attack is to prove this coincident-frame comparability lemma. Once you have that, the septic quotient rung is no longer independent.

That is the cleanest continuation of the septic attack I can justify from the current picture.

_Thought for 1m 56s_

I think this lemma now breaks into a **formal half** and a **geometric half**, and the formal half is essentially done.

The strong two-point route is only asking for the order-\(7\) class in
\[

\]
so the septic target is already the weaker quotient statement

\]
equivalently
\[
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]
That is exactly the package the strong finite-order criterion was built to use. 

Here is the formal half.

Suppose two corrected odd germs, already projected to the residual fixed-sector level, have expansions
\[
\Gamma_2(s)=c\,s^3+U\,s^5+V_2\,s^7+O(s^9),
\qquad
\Gamma_1(\sigma)=c\,\sigma^3+U\,\sigma^5+V_1\,\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\]
where \(c\) is the common cubic scalar channel and \(U=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)\) is the common quintic fixed-sector coefficient after lower-order merger.

Assume
\[
s=\chi(\sigma)=\sigma+\alpha \sigma^3+\beta \sigma^5+O(\sigma^7)
\]
is an odd invertible reparametrization. Then
\[
s^3=\sigma^3+3\alpha \sigma^5+(3\beta+3\alpha^2)\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\]
\[
s^5=\sigma^5+5\alpha \sigma^7+O(\sigma^9),
\qquad
s^7=\sigma^7+O(\sigma^9).
\]

\[
\Gamma_2(\chi(\sigma))
=
c\,\sigma^3
+
\bigl(U+3\alpha\,c\bigr)\sigma^5
+
\bigl(V_2+5\alpha U +(3\beta+3\alpha^2)c\bigr)\sigma^7
+
O(\sigma^9).
\]

After modding out the lower scalar/value gauge, the only order-\(7\) fixed-sector drift is
\[
V_2\longmapsto V_2+5\alpha U.
\]
Therefore the quotient class
\[
[V]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C U
\]
is invariant under the residual odd reparametrization freedom once cubic and quintic order have been matched.

So the **formal statement** is proved:

> If the coincident two-pair and total-amplitude one-pair germs differ only by odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower scalar/value gauge after cubic/quintic merger, then the septic quotient defect vanishes automatically:
> \[
> \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
> \]

That is the whole septic calculation. No additional order-\(7\) miracle is needed.

So the actual remaining content of the lemma is smaller than it first looked.

What remains is the **geometric half**:

> after cubic/quintic lower-order merger on coincident atoms, the actual corrected two-pair germ and the actual corrected one-pair total-amplitude germ represent the same local corrected image germ, so they differ only by odd local parameter choice.

That is the real bottleneck.

I would phrase it even more sharply:

### Reduced lemma
After cubic/quintic lower-order merger on coincident atoms, the corrected coincident two-pair germ and the corrected one-pair total-amplitude germ define the same reduced one-dimensional analytic image germ in the lower-gauge quotient.

Because if that is true, then normalization of a reduced one-dimensional analytic germ gives a local analytic reparametrization between the two parametrizations. Since both parametrizations are odd and have cubic leading order, the reparametrization can be taken odd with
\[
\chi(\sigma)=\sigma+O(\sigma^3),
\]
and then the septic quotient collapse follows from the substitution calculation above.

So the attack has now reduced the septic burden to this:

1. prove **same image germ at coincidence** after cubic/quintic merger;
2. then odd reparametrization follows formally;
3. then the septic quotient class agrees automatically.

That is a real reduction. It means the septic rung is no longer an independent analytic order-\(7\) identity to prove by hand.

There is also a useful strategic consequence.

For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, the already-proved good-patch closeness corollary only uses the cubic and quintic defects, so this septic work is not needed for that local contradiction. turn55file9

For the **strong source-level merger route**, this septic reduction matters a lot, because it says the order-\(7\) input is not “prove full septic equality,” but only “prove image-germ coincidence up to odd frame change after lower-order merger.” That is a much smaller and more natural theorem than a standalone septic identity. turn55file4

So my current best attack is:

- stop treating the septic rung as separate data;
- prove the cubic/quintic merger first;
- then prove the **coincident image-germ lemma**;
- then the order-\(7\) quotient collapse is formal.

That is the sharpest version of the argument I can defend right now.

\[

\]
and the corollary proving two-point exclusion from the strong route still uses the full \(3/5/7\) package. L1462-L1480 L1488-L1495

So lower-order merger alone does **not** imply the lemma. The order-\(7\) transverse class is exactly the obstruction.

> After cubic/quintic lower-order merger on coincident atoms, the actual corrected two-pair germ and the actual corrected one-pair total-amplitude germ define the **same reduced one-dimensional analytic image germ** in the lower-gauge quotient.

\[
s=\chi(\sigma)=\sigma+O(\sigma^3).
\]
Then the substitution calculation above shows immediately that the order-\(7\) mismatch is pure gauge:
\[
V_2-V_1\in \mathbf C U,
\]
so the septic quotient defect vanishes on the diagonal.

So the attack has reduced the coincident-frame lemma to an even smaller statement:

\[
\boxed{\text{same reduced image germ at coincidence}}
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{\text{odd reparametrization comparability}}
\Longrightarrow
\boxed{\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=0.}

That is the cleanest point we have reached.

\[

\]
so the septic quotient class is not part of that local contradiction. 1. Stop trying to deduce the lemma from cubic/quintic jets alone. That is false in general.

\]
so cubic and quintic are enough there; the septic quotient class is not part of that local exclusion theorem. L151-L223

For the **strong finite-order source-level route**, the septic quotient rung remains part of the package, but it is now no longer an independent diagonal identity. It is a formal consequence of same-image-germ comparability, if that can be proved. L1462-L1480

So the best continuation of the attack is:

1. stop trying to squeeze the lemma out of cubic/quintic jets alone;
2. prove that at coincidence the corrected two-pair and total-amplitude one-pair constructions define the same reduced image germ in the lower-gauge quotient;
3. then the odd frame change is automatic;
4. then the septic quotient collapse follows formally.

That is the smallest honest theorem still standing between the strong \(3/5/7\) route and the order-\(7\) diagonal identity.

The most likely place to push next is the corrected-block construction itself: if one can show that, on the collision family, both constructions are just two local parameter choices on the same reduced one-dimensional corrected image, then the septic rung is finished.
## User (2026-04-21 16:42:41)

continue your attack

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:42:46)

I’m pushing directly on the only honest remaining step now: whether collision in the corrected-block construction forces the two-atom and total-amplitude one-atom models to land on the same reduced local image germ, rather than merely matching a couple of jets.

_Thought for 2m 41s_

I think the attack now turns in a useful way:

the **same-image-germ lemma is probably easier than the full source-level merger theorem**, because it only asks for **collision functoriality**, not one-atom linearity in amplitude.

That matters because the earlier no-go against the naive source-summed corrected package only killed the strong linear statement
\[
Q(a\delta_h)=a\,Q(\delta_h).
\]
It did **not** kill the weaker collision statement
\[
Q(a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h)=Q((a_1+a_2)\delta_h).
\]
Those are very different. The strong finite-order route still needs the full \(3/5/7\) package and additivity-type structure, while the residual-corner route only needs the cubic/quintic defects on a compact good patch.  

So here is the next, sharper attack.

## 1. Replace the image-germ lemma by a stronger pre-whitening collision lemma

The most natural object is not the final quotient germ, but the corrected block triple before whitening:
\[
\mathcal B_\mu(s):=
\bigl(G^{\corr}_{\mu,-}(s),\,N^{\corr}_{\mu}(s),\,G^{\corr}_{\mu,+}(s)\bigr).
\]

If the actual corrected two-pair construction really factors through the local source fields
\[
q_\mu,\qquad \Phi_\mu,\qquad \Delta_{\mu,m}(s)
:=\Phi_\mu\!\left(m-\frac s2\right)-\Phi_\mu\!\left(m+\frac s2\right),
\]
then on the diagonal source
\[
\mu=a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h
\]
we get **exact equality of inputs**, hence exact equality of corrected block germs:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h}(s)
=
\mathcal B_{(a_1+a_2)\delta_h}(s).
}
\]

This is much stronger than “same image germ,” and if it is true then the rest is formal.

Why? Because whitening is an analytic map
\[
\mathcal W:(G_-,N,G_+)\longmapsto G_-^{-1/2}NG_+^{-1/2},
\]
so exact equality of corrected block germs implies exact equality of the whitened germs:
\[
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h}(s)
=
\widehat\Omega^{\corr}_{(a_1+a_2)\delta_h}(s).
\]
Then certainly they define the same reduced image germ; in fact they are literally the same germ in the same parameter. So the whole “odd reparametrization comparability” business becomes unnecessary if collision functoriality holds at the block level. This is the cleanest way to attack the lemma. 

## 2. Why this does not conflict with the even-amplitude no-go

This is the important conceptual point.

Earlier we learned that the naive source-summed whitened package is **not** linear in the one-atom weight \(a\), so it cannot prove the full interaction factorization route. That remains true. But collision functoriality is weaker: it only says that when the two atoms actually coincide, the construction depends on the combined source
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
not on the presentation as two separate labels. That does **not** require linearity of the one-atom path in \(a\). Even an even-in-\(a\) one-atom package can still satisfy exact collision invariance. So the earlier negative finding does not block this lemma. It only blocks the stronger “full source-level merger gives interaction remainder factorization” route. 

That is why this is the right place to push.

## 3. What exact theorem now remains

The same-image-germ lemma can now be reduced to this very concrete statement:

> **Collision functoriality for corrected blocks.**  
> The actual corrected two-pair local block construction depends only on the underlying source \(\mu\) on the collision locus, so that for
> \[
> \mu=a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h
> \]
> one has
> \[
> G^{\corr}_{\mu,\pm}(s)=G^{\corr}_{(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,\pm}(s),
> \qquad
> N^{\corr}_{\mu}(s)=N^{\corr}_{(a_1+a_2)\delta_h}(s)
> \]
> as local germs.

If that theorem is true, then:

1. the whitened germs coincide exactly;
2. the cubic scalar and quintic fixed-sector terms coincide automatically;
3. the order-\(7\) fixed-sector terms coincide up to the already-quotiented \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge automatically;
4. hence
   \[
   \overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
   \]

So the septic quotient diagonal-collapse problem is reduced to collision functoriality of the pre-whitened blocks, not to a new septic computation. That is a real simplification.

## 4. What is genuinely still missing

The honest gap is this:

I do not yet see, from the current draft alone, that the **actual** corrected two-pair object used downstream is already defined as a source-functorial block construction on the collision locus. If it is, the lemma is basically done. If it is not, then the remaining work is to prove just this restricted source-presentation invariance:
presentation-independence only for
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
not for all separated two-atom data.

That is much smaller than full source-definedness on arbitrary finite atomic measures. It is exactly the “collision” piece of the original source-level theorem. And it is the only piece needed to get the same-image-germ statement and hence the septic quotient diagonal collapse.

## 5. What this means tactically

So the attack now splits cleanly.

For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, the local exclusion theorem still only needs the cubic and quintic defects through the good-patch closeness estimate, so this septic work is not needed there. turn64file5

For the **strong finite-order route**, the septic quotient rung is now no longer a separate mystery. It is a consequence of the single collision-functoriality lemma above.

That means the best next attack is no longer “prove the image-germ lemma” or “prove a septic identity.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove collision functoriality of the corrected block triple on }a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h.
}
\]

If you get that, the same-image-germ lemma follows immediately, and the septic quotient defect dies on the diagonal.

That is as far as I can honestly push it from the current material: the septic problem has been reduced to a very concrete collision invariance statement at the pre-whitening level.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:47:22)

I’m testing the strongest remaining reduction against the actual TeX now: whether the corrected same-point/cross-block formulas already depend only on the combined source on the collision locus, which would make the septic diagonal collapse essentially formal.

_Thought for 35s_

Yes — the attack sharpens again, and it changes the target in an important way.

The strongest correction is this: for actual close two-point bad cores on a good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the relevant “collision” is **not** the full diagonal
\[
(h_1,h_2,\lambda)=(h,h,\text{arbitrary}),
\]
but the **collision-cancellation locus**
\[
\delta:=h_2-h_1=0,\qquad \lambda:= -\frac{a_2}{a_1}=1.
\]
That is because the cubic cancellation condition forces
\[
a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)\approx 0,
\]
so when \(h_1\approx h_2\) and \(c\neq 0\), one must have \(a_1+a_2\approx 0\), i.e. \(\lambda\approx 1\). So the right local model is not “coincident atoms with arbitrary total amplitude,” but “coincident atoms with zero total amplitude to first order.” 

That means the collision-functoriality lemma should be attacked in a **blown-up cancellation chart**, not on the raw diagonal.

Write
\[
\mu:=\lambda-1,\qquad
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2}.
\]
If \(D_h:=(q_h,\Phi_h)\) denotes the local datum, then the branch datum is
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\mu D_m-\delta D_m'+O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr).
\]
Equivalently, after polar blow-up
\[
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
one gets
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\rho\bigl(\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'\bigr)+O(\rho^2).
\]
So the local cancellation family is controlled not by the raw pair \((a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\) separately, but by the **projective source direction**
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}:=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
That is the clean attack formula. 

This matters because it shows why ordinary Taylor expansion at zero source is the wrong model: the corrected same-point and mixed blocks are \(O(\rho)\), but whitening contributes \(O(\rho^{-1/2})\) on each side, so the whitened object is \(O(1)\). In other words, the local model is scale-invariant after whitening, and the right limit is a **blown-up limit family** depending only on the source direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\), not on the overall scale \(\rho\). That is exactly the same scale-cancellation obstruction already seen in the one-atom analysis. 

So the next honest theorem is no longer the broad “same reduced image germ at coincidence” statement for arbitrary coincident presentations. It becomes this smaller and more natural one:

> **Cancellation-blow-up universality lemma.**  
> Near the collision-cancellation locus \((\delta,\mu)=(0,0)\), the corrected local construction through the relevant finite order depends only on the blown-up projective source direction
> \[
> \Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
> \]
> Equivalently, after dividing out the scale \(\rho\), the cubic/quintic (and, for the strong route, septic quotient) witnesses admit limits depending only on \((m,\theta)\), not on the particular presentation of the nearby cancelling two-atom datum. 

This is better than the earlier lemma for two reasons.

First, it matches the **actual asymptotic regime** of close bad cores: \(\delta\to 0\) and \(\lambda\to 1\), not arbitrary diagonal merger. 

Second, it bypasses the dead amplitude-linear route. The conversation already isolated that the wrong target was “prove amplitude-linear decomposition,” while the right target is to promote the corrected local construction to a **general local-datum functor** and then apply it to the summed/cancelling local datum. In that formulation, source-functoriality becomes almost tautological. 

So the continued attack looks like this.

For the **local cubic/quintic residual-corner route**, the best theorem is probably:

1. promote the corrected local construction to an abstract local-datum cubic/quintic functor;
2. show the blow-up limits
   \[
   C_0(m,\theta),\qquad Q_0(m,\theta)
   \]
   exist and depend only on \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\);
3. then exact close two-point residual branches are governed by a one-directional projective source datum, not by two independent atoms. That is exactly the right structure to force evenness and diagonal vanishing on the involutive residual corner. turn66file1

For the **strong \(3/5/7\) route**, the septic quotient defect should then be attacked in the same blown-up framework: not as full order-\(7\) equality of coincident germs, but as quotient-invariance of the order-\(7\) class under the same projective source-direction reduction. If the order-\(\le 7\) corrected object is functorial in the local datum, then on the collision-cancellation blow-up the only surviving order-\(7\) ambiguity is the existing \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-gauge, so the septic quotient class should become presentation-independent automatically. That is the natural continuation of the earlier septic reduction. turn66file3turn66file4

So the attack has changed in a useful way:

the remaining theorem is probably **not** “arbitrary coincident-frame comparability.”  
It is the more specific and more realistic **blown-up cancellation functoriality** theorem near
\[
(\delta,\lambda-1)=(0,0),
\]
with the corrected witnesses depending only on the projective local source direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\). That is the smallest theorem that matches the actual bad-branch asymptotics and dodges the earlier no-go.

_Thought for 28s_

Yes — this is genuinely relevant, and it sharpens the picture in a useful way.

The main gain is that it pushes the residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
from “an involutive quotient-diagonal branch” to a much stronger statement: every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\), and on the first live quartic–sextic rung \((m,n)=(4,6)\iff(r,e)=(2,0)\), the whole finite transport state is locally a function of the single scalar \(Q\) alone. In that sense the residual transport package has local rank \(1\), not two independent local degrees of freedom.  

That matters because it upgrades the old “even scalar” picture into a **finite transport-state quotient descent theorem** and then a **no finite-order hidden reset theorem**: on the quartic–sextic rung, equality of any finite descended transport state can only identify the involution pair \(t\leftrightarrow -t\), and cannot create a third local reset. So any still-live obstruction on the residual corner cannot come from hidden finite-order behavior inside the quotient-visible transport jets themselves.  

For our current two-point work, the most important consequence is the conditional closure statement. If the actual corrected cubic/quintic residual defects are analytic functionals of a finite quotient-visible transport state, then along the involutive branch they are automatically \(O(t^2)\), hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
which is exactly the scale needed for the existing defect-closeness exclusion mechanism on a compact good patch. And if the full two-pair package is state-local with the natural diagonal merger law, then the interaction remainder vanishes identically along the involutive branch.  

So this handback strongly supports one part of our current attack: it reinforces that the residual corner is no longer a geometry problem in any ordinary sense. The geometry has already been compressed to a quotient-visible rank-one transport state. If the corner is still live, the obstruction must come from something **beyond** the descended one-atom transport state: genuinely relational two-atom data, provenance-sensitive data, or some non-finite-order dependence. That lines up extremely well with our own conclusion that the remaining bottleneck is package-level and possibly relational, not “more local transport geometry.”  

Where I would be careful is this: it does **not** by itself close the strong source-level \(3/5/7\) route. The handback gives a strong conditional theorem of the form “if the actual defects/package are state-local in the descended transport variables, then the corner closes,” but it does not prove that the actual corrected two-pair package really is state-local in that sense. The note itself is explicit that this is the remaining gap. So I would treat it as a powerful narrowing of the residual-corner route, not as a full closure of two-point.  

Relative to our recent septic work, I think the clean synthesis is this. For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, this new handback makes the septic quotient defect even less central: the local contradiction route only needs cubic and quintic defects if they are state-local or package-local in the quotient-visible transport state. For the **stronger global source-level route**, the septic quotient rung still matters, but this handback suggests exactly where any failure must live: not inside the descended transport jets, but in the first genuinely relational/provenance-sensitive two-atom input that survives transport descent. That is a meaningful refinement of the frontier.  

So my verdict is: this is a real strengthening of the residual-corner story, and I would absolutely fold it into the draft. It does not replace our current package-level attack, but it sharpens it by saying that if two-point is still open on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
the missing ingredient is not hidden inside the quotient-visible transport state. It must be the first genuinely relational two-atom datum beyond that state.

Here’s the handback I’d send.

The two-point picture is now much sharper than when we started. I think the right global summary is that there are still three conditional routes, but the mixed residual corner has been compressed much more than the draft currently reflects: the strong finite-order route is still the cubic/quintic/septic package with diagonal merger; the weaker exact route is a genuine corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse; and the mixed route is now the \(\lambda\)-sheared projective-shadow route on a good overlap patch. The naive source-summed corrected-block route is dead: the raw corrected whitened block is even in the source weight, so it cannot supply the required linear merger law, while the one-atom source-weight path is nevertheless invisible in the ambient quotient \(\Qabs\). That is the right replacement for the failed raw linearity statement.   

On the mixed side, the overlap geometry is now fully split. The branch can accumulate only on \(\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}\), with \((K_v=0,S\neq 0)\) already absorbed by the mixed low-order obstruction package, \((S=0,K_v\neq 0)\) already transferred into nonmixed \(4\)-point geometry, and only the residual exact fixed-shear corner \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\) genuinely left. On that corner, after parity reduction, the local branch is involutive / quotient-diagonal, \(Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)\), the residual ladder is even-support over \(K_v=0\), and on the first surviving quartic–sextic rung \((m,n)=(4,6)\iff(r,e)=(2,0)\), the quotient scalar is already locally injective in \(u=t^2\). So local exact fixed-shear re-entry is already gone at that rung.  

The biggest new gain from the residual-corner attack is stronger than “one even scalar descends.” Every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends analytically to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\). On the quartic–sextic rung, every such finite transport jet is actually an analytic function of the single scalar \(Q\) alone, so the whole finite transport state has local rank \(1\). From that one gets a no-finite-order-hidden-reset theorem: equality of any finite quotient-visible transport state can only identify the involution pair \(t\leftrightarrow -t\), and cannot create a third local reset. So if the residual corner is still live, the obstruction cannot come from hidden finite-order behavior inside the quotient-visible transport state itself.   

That leads to the cleanest conditional closures I found. In the weaker form: if the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects are analytic functionals of a finite quotient-visible transport state and vanish on the diagonal state, then along the involutive branch they are \(O(t^2)\), hence \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and the already-proved good-patch defect-closeness mechanism excludes the branch. In the stronger form: if the full corrected two-pair package is state-local in the two descended one-atom transport states and satisfies the natural merger law \(\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y,Y)=(a_1+a_2)\mathfrak F(Y)\), then on the involutive branch the interaction remainder actually vanishes identically. So the real remaining question on the residual corner is not more local geometry; it is whether the actual corrected package is finite-state-local, or whether some genuinely relational/provenance-sensitive two-atom datum survives transport descent.   

I also think the right division between the residual-corner route and the strong source-level route is now clear. For the residual exact fixed-shear corner, the prototype local exclusion theorem only needs the cubic and quintic defects: evenness plus diagonal vanishing gives \(E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and the existing good-patch corollary already closes the branch from those two quantities alone. So septic is not central there. By contrast, for the stronger finite-order source-level merger route, the septic quotient class still matters, because that route is explicitly organized around the full cubic/quintic/septic package through order \(7\).  L1462-L1480

On the septic side, the attack reduced the target substantially. The order-\(7\) datum that matters is not full septic equality, but only the quotient class in \(\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). Formally, once two corrected germs agree through cubic and quintic order and differ only by an odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower scalar/value gauge, the order-\(7\) mismatch is automatically a multiple of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), so the septic quotient defect vanishes. But there is also a sharp negative finding: cubic/quintic jet merger alone does not force odd-reparametrization comparability; the transverse order-\(7\) quotient class is exactly the obstruction. So the honest remaining septic theorem is not “prove order-\(7\) equality,” but “prove same reduced image germ at coincidence,” or, even better, prove collision-functoriality at the corrected-block level on the collision/cancellation locus so that the same-image-germ statement becomes formal. L1462-L1480

My best current synthesis is therefore this. The exact fixed-shear residual corner is now much more rigid than before: the branch is quotient-diagonal / involutive, the whole finite transport package is quotient-visible, on the first live rung it has local rank \(1\), and no hidden finite-order reset survives there. So if the corner is still live, the obstruction must come from the first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom input that survives after quotient-visible transport descent, not from any descended one-atom transport state alone. In other words: the remaining burden is package-level and relational, not geometric. That is the main handback.  

If I were telling the nonmixed \(4\)-point chat what is most useful to do with this, I’d say: treat the residual mixed corner as no longer a free local branch problem. The geometry is already compressed to a rank-one quotient-visible transport state; any further obstruction must be relational/provenance-sensitive. So if their nonmixed \(4\)-point work can identify or eliminate the first genuinely relational two-atom datum that survives after descent, that is exactly the kind of input that now looks decisive for the remaining \(2\)-point burden.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:55:17)

I’m consolidating the math into one coherent package now: the surviving routes, the hard negative findings, the residual-corner structure, and the smallest remaining theorem statements.

_Thought for 1m 6s_

Here is the full mathematical picture I think we now understand from this attack.

The two-point problem has separated into three distinct conditional routes. The first is the strong finite-order source-level merger route: build the actual corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package on small two-atom data with swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h,
\]
which would force the quadratic interaction factorization and hence the defect-scale contradiction on good patches. The second is the weaker exact quotient-diagonal route: a genuine corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse would already exclude exact close bad two-point cores on compact subsets of \(\{c\neq 0\}\). The third is the mixed \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow route on a good overlap patch. Those are the only live \(2\)-point lanes I still see. 

The algebraic heart of the strong route is now completely clear. If one has an analytic two-atom package with swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger, then the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
automatically factors as
\[
\mathcal I_2=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]
That formal divisibility argument is not the issue anymore. The genuine open theorem is source-level or package-level: one must prove that the actual corrected finite-order package is defined in the right way on two-atom data and collapses correctly on coincident atoms. 

A decisive negative finding is also now clear: the naive source-summed corrected-block route cannot prove the strong theorem. Along a weighted one-atom path, its extracted finite-order coefficients are even analytic in the source weight, so the required linear merger law cannot come from that model. This kills the earlier “obvious source-linear closure” route, but it does not kill weaker collision or package-level functoriality statements.  

On the mixed side, the overlap geometry has become much sharper. After freezing a \(\lambda\)-shear subsequence, the projective secant shadow can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Within that union, the picture is now split: \((K_v=0,S\neq 0)\) is already in the mixed low-order obstruction regime, \((S=0,K_v\neq 0)\) transfers into nonmixed \(4\)-point geometry, and the only genuinely residual derivative-geometric corner is
\[
S=0,\qquad K_v=0.
\]
That is one of the main structural gains of the whole attack.  

On that residual exact fixed-shear corner, the branch is no longer a free two-point branch. After centering and reparametrization, the local projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad m\ \text{even},\quad G(-t)=G(t),
\]
so
\[
\Phi(t)=\Phi(-t),
\qquad
\Phi(t)=\widehat\Phi(t^2).
\]
Thus the residual branch is quotient-diagonal and involutive. The associated transport scalar
\[
Q(t):=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}
\]
is even,
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
and the residual ladder satisfies
\[
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),\qquad
q-r=2e+2,\qquad m=r+2,\qquad n=r+2e+4.
\]
So the whole residual exact fixed-shear lane sits on an even-support ladder over \(K_v=0\), while the source Wronskian still vanishes to odd order. 

At the first surviving rung,
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0),
\]
one has \(\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0\), so \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective in the quotient variable \(u=t^2\). That gives a real no-go: there is no local exact fixed-shear re-entry after quotienting the involution on the quartic–sextic rung.  

I then pushed this much further. If one defines parity-normalized transport jets
\[
\Theta_k(t):=t^{-(k\bmod 2)}Q^{(k)}(t),
\]
then each \(\Theta_k\) is again even analytic and therefore descends to a quotient germ in \(u=t^2\). This gives a finite transport-jet quotient descent theorem: every finite parity-normalized transport jet on the exact fixed-shear involutive branch is quotient-visible. On the quartic–sextic rung this sharpens further, because \(\widehat Q\) is then a local coordinate in \(u\), so every descended jet is actually an analytic function of the single scalar \(Q\) itself. In that sense the entire finite transport state has local rank \(1\).  

From that, one gets a no-finite-order-hidden-reset theorem. If
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t))
\]
is any finite quotient-visible transport state, then on the quartic–sextic rung equality \(\mathcal T_N(t_1)=\mathcal T_N(t_2)\) forces \(t_2=\pm t_1\). So the only local duplication in any finite descended transport state is the known involution pair, and there is no third local reset point. This rules out a whole class of hidden-state mechanisms on the residual corner. 

That leads to the most useful conditional closures I found. In a weaker form: if the actual corrected cubic/quintic residual defects are analytic functionals of a finite quotient-visible transport state and vanish on the diagonal state, then
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t),\ E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2),
\]
hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
because \(h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3)\). The already-proved good-patch defect-closeness estimate then excludes the branch. In a stronger form: if the full corrected two-pair package is state-local in the two individual descended one-atom transport states and obeys the natural merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y,Y)=(a_1+a_2)\mathfrak F(Y),
\]
then on the involutive branch the interaction remainder vanishes identically.  

This yields the sharpest negative finding of the residual-corner attack. If the exact fixed-shear corner \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\) is still genuinely live, then the obstruction cannot come from any hidden finite-order behavior inside the quotient-visible transport jet itself. More concretely, it cannot come from a second local transport variable on the quartic–sextic rung, cannot come from a third reset inside any finite descended transport state, and cannot come from a two-pair model built only from the two separate quotient-visible one-atom states, assuming the natural merger law. Any still-live obstruction must therefore come from the first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom input that survives after quotient-visible transport descent, or from some non-finite-order dependence. That is the cleanest “what remains” theorem-level conclusion I have.  

There was also an important correction to the earlier diagonal-merger viewpoint. Near a genuine close two-point bad branch on a good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the relevant limiting locus is not the ordinary diagonal \((h_1,h_2)=(h,h)\) with arbitrary total amplitude, but the collision-cancellation locus
\[
\delta:=h_2-h_1=0,\qquad \lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}=1.
\]
Indeed, the cubic identity forces \(a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)\approx 0\), so when \(h_1\approx h_2\) and \(c\neq 0\), one must have \(a_1+a_2\approx 0\), i.e. \(\lambda\approx 1\). On that locus the combined source tends to zero, not to a one-atom source, so continuity to a one-atom diagonal object was aimed at the wrong base point. This is why the old quadratic-factorization target is the wrong chart for the cancellation regime.  

In that chart one should instead set
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta:=h_2-h_1,\qquad \mu:=\lambda-1,
\]
and blow up the cancellation locus \((\mu,\delta)=(0,0)\). The local branch datum then has the form
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\mu D_m-\delta D_m'+O((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2),
\]
so after polar blow-up \((\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta)\) the effective projective source direction is
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}:=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
That is the right local datum near a close cancelling two-point branch. The best replacement for the old quadratic theorem is then a blown-up cubic/quintic limit theorem: after projectivization, the corrected witnesses should have limits depending only on \((m,\theta)\), i.e. only on the projective source direction \(\Theta_{m,\theta}\). This is compatible with the even-in-amplitude obstruction and the scale cancellation in whitening, and it matches the actual geometry of close bad two-point cores.  

This blown-up chart also gives the correct “first-order interaction” viewpoint. The live problem is no longer “prove \(O(\rho^2)\)” on the cancellation chart. It is to identify or constrain the first blow-up law of the actual interaction defects near \((\mu,\delta)=(0,0)\), and show that it cannot realize the naive tangent-direction family on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\). That is where the one-pair geometry re-enters via the linear independence of \((c,A_5^{\mathfrak f})\) and its derivative when \(M\neq 0\).  

Finally, on the order-\(7\) side, the septic quantity that matters globally is only the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
not full equality of septic representatives. Formally, once two corrected germs agree through cubic and quintic order and differ only by an odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower scalar/value gauge, the order-\(7\) mismatch is automatically a multiple of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), so the septic quotient defect vanishes. But cubic/quintic jet merger alone does not force that odd-reparametrization comparability; the transverse order-\(7\) quotient class is exactly the obstruction. So the honest septic theorem is not “prove order-\(7\) equality,” but either prove same reduced image germ at coincidence or, more concretely, prove collision functoriality for the corrected block triple on the collision/cancellation locus. If that weaker collision-functoriality theorem holds, then the same-image-germ statement and the septic quotient collapse become formal. 

So the whole progress, in one sentence, is this: the two-point problem is no longer blocked by generic local geometry. The geometry has already compressed the residual mixed corner to a quotient-diagonal, rank-one, finite-state-visible transport problem with no hidden finite-order reset. The remaining burden is package-level: either prove the finite-order source-level merger theorem, or prove state-locality / collision-functoriality of the actual corrected two-pair package, or prove that the first genuinely relational two-atom datum surviving after quotient-visible transport descent cannot realize the required bad-branch interaction.

## 1) Insert a collision-cancellation chart remark in the two-point section

Insert this **immediately after** the end of

```latex
\begin{remark}[Affine freezing is stronger than projective freezing on the mixed two-point branch]
\label{rem:affine-freezing-stronger-than-projective-two-point}

\end{remark}
```

Use:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Collision-cancellation chart for close two-point cores]
\label{rem:wip-collision-cancellation-chart-two-point}
On a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0\},
\]
a close exact two-point bad core is naturally studied not in the raw diagonal
chart \((h_1,h_2)\to(h,h)\), but in the cancellation chart
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
\delta:=h_2-h_1,
\qquad
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
\mu:=\lambda-1.
\]
Indeed, the cubic equation
\[
a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)=0
\]
forces \(\lambda\to 1\) whenever \(\delta\to 0\) on \(J\).

Writing
\[
\mathcal D_h:=(c(h),u_5(h),v_5(h)),
\]
one has the first-order expansion
\[
\mathcal D_{h_1}-\lambda \mathcal D_{h_2}
=
-\mu\,\mathcal D_m-\delta\,\mathcal D_m'
+
O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr).
\]
After polar blow-up
\[
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
the leading cancellation datum is therefore the projective source direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}
:=
\cos\theta\,\mathcal D_m+\sin\theta\,\mathcal D_m'.
\]

So any future cubic/quintic limit theorem for close cancelling two-point cores
should be phrased in this blown-up collision-cancellation chart rather than as a
Taylor expansion through the singular zero-source point.
\end{remark}
```

This captures the later realization that the correct local chart near a close bad two-point branch is the **collision-cancellation** blow-up \((\mu,\delta)\to(0,0)\), not the raw coincident-source chart. 

## 2) Insert the finite transport-state package after the quartic–sextic no-reentry corollary

Insert this **immediately after** the proof of

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Quartic--sextic quotient injectivity and local no-reentry]
\label{cor:quartic-sextic-quotient-injectivity-local-no-reentry}
...
\end{corollary}
```

and **before** `\begin{remark}[Quotient-cusp interpretation and the no-reset issue]`.

Use:

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Finite transport-jet quotient descent on the exact fixed-shear corner]
\label{prop:finite-transport-jet-quotient-descent-fixed-shear-corner}
Assume the additional conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane from
Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}, and work
along a local involutive branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)).
\]
For each \(k\ge 0\), define the parity-normalized transport jet
\[
\Theta_k(t):=
\begin{cases}
Q^{(k)}(t),& k\ \text{even},\\[4pt]
t^{-1}Q^{(k)}(t),& k\ \text{odd},
\end{cases}
\]
where
\[
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Then every \(\Theta_k\) is even analytic. Equivalently, for each \(k\ge 0\)
there exists a unique analytic quotient germ \(\widetilde\Theta_k(u)\) such that
\[
\Theta_k(t)=\widetilde\Theta_k(t^2).
\]
In particular, the canonical descended scalar
\[
X(t):=\frac{Q'(t)}{t}
\]
is even analytic and satisfies
\[
X(t)=2\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since \(Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)\) is even, \(Q^{(k)}\) has the usual parity:
\(Q^{(k)}\) is even for \(k\) even and odd for \(k\) odd. Every odd analytic
germ is divisible by \(t\), so \(\Theta_k\) is analytic for odd \(k\). In both
cases \(\Theta_k\) is even, hence factors uniquely through \(u=t^2\). The final
identity is immediate from
\[
Q'(t)=2t\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Rank-one quotient-visible transport state on the quartic--sextic rung]
\label{cor:rank-one-transport-state-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear}
Assume the quartic--sextic residual case
\[
(m,n)=(4,6).
\]
For every \(N\ge 0\), set
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t)).
\]
Then there exists an analytic map
\[
\mathbf F_N
\]
defined near \(Q(0)\) such that
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathbf F_N(Q(t)).
\]
Equivalently, every finite quotient-visible transport state is locally an
analytic function of the single scalar \(Q\) alone.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By
Corollary~\ref{cor:quartic-sextic-quotient-injectivity-local-no-reentry},
\(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in \(u=t^2\). Since each
\(\Theta_k(t)=\widetilde\Theta_k(t^2)\), each descended jet
\(\widetilde\Theta_k(u)\) can be re-expressed analytically as a function of
\(\widehat Q(u)\), hence of \(Q(t)\). Stacking these functions gives
\(\mathbf F_N\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[No finite-order hidden reset on the quartic--sextic residual corner]
\label{cor:no-finite-order-hidden-reset-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear}
Assume the quartic--sextic residual case. Let
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t))
\]
be any finite quotient-visible transport state. Then
\[
\mathcal T_N(t_1)=\mathcal T_N(t_2)
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
t_2=\pm t_1.
\]
In particular, no finite quotient-visible transport state produces a third local
reset beyond the involution symmetry \(t\leftrightarrow -t\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By
Corollary~\ref{cor:rank-one-transport-state-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear},
equality of \(\mathcal T_N\) implies equality of \(Q\). But
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
and
Corollary~\ref{cor:quartic-sextic-quotient-injectivity-local-no-reentry}
shows that \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective in \(u=t^2\). Hence
\(t_1^2=t_2^2\), so \(t_2=\pm t_1\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Conditional state-local defect closure on the residual exact fixed-shear corner]
\label{prop:conditional-state-local-defect-closure-fixed-shear-corner}
Assume the setup of
Proposition~\ref{prop:residual-involutive-defect-criterion-fixed-shear-corner}.
Suppose there exists \(N\ge 0\) and analytic functionals
\[
\mathfrak e_3,\mathfrak e_5
\]
defined near \(\mathcal T_N(0)\) such that along the involutive branch
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\mathfrak e_3(\mathcal T_N(t)),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\mathfrak e_5(\mathcal T_N(t)),
\]
and
\[
\mathfrak e_3(\mathcal T_N(0))=\mathfrak e_5(\mathcal T_N(0))=0.
\]
Then
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2),
\]
hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
and no such nontrivial exact residual fixed-shear involutive bad branch can
persist on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-transport-jet-quotient-descent-fixed-shear-corner},
each \(\Theta_k\) is even analytic, so
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathcal T_N(0)+O(t^2).
\]
Analyticity of \(\mathfrak e_3,\mathfrak e_5\) and vanishing at \(\mathcal T_N(0)\)
therefore give
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
this becomes
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
Now apply Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Stronger conditional package collapse on the involutive branch]
\label{cor:stronger-state-local-package-collapse-fixed-shear-corner}
Assume the setup of
Proposition~\ref{prop:residual-involutive-defect-criterion-fixed-shear-corner}.
Suppose that for some \(N\ge 0\) the corrected two-pair package along the
involutive branch is state-local in the sense that
\[
\mathcal P_2(t)
=
\mathfrak P_2\bigl(a_1(t),a_2(t);\mathcal T_N(t),\mathcal T_N(t)\bigr),
\]
and the corresponding one-pair package is
\[
F_{h_1(t)}=F_{h_2(t)}=\mathfrak F(\mathcal T_N(t)).
\]
Assume moreover the natural merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y,Y)=(a_1+a_2)\mathfrak F(Y).
\]
Then the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(t):=
\mathcal P_2(t)-a_1(t)F_{h_1(t)}-a_2(t)F_{h_2(t)}
\]
vanishes identically along the involutive branch:
\[
\mathcal I_2(t)\equiv 0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Substitute the displayed state-local forms into the definition of
\(\mathcal I_2(t)\), then apply the merger law with \(Y=\mathcal T_N(t)\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Any remaining residual obstruction is genuinely relational]
\label{rem:any-remaining-residual-obstruction-is-genuinely-relational}
The preceding results show that on the quartic--sextic residual corner the
finite quotient-visible transport state has local rank \(1\) and no finite-order
hidden reset. Therefore, if the exact fixed-shear residual corner is still
genuinely live, the obstruction cannot come from:
\begin{itemize}
\item a second local transport variable on the quartic--sextic rung;
\item a third local reset inside any finite quotient-visible transport state; or
\item a two-pair model built only from the descended one-atom transport state,
assuming the natural merger law.
\end{itemize}
So any still-live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
must come from the first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom
input that survives after quotient-visible transport descent, or else from
non-finite-order dependence.
\end{remark}
```

This is the main new theorem package from the attack: the finite transport-jet descent, the quartic–sextic rank-one compression, the no-hidden-reset consequence, and the conditional state-local closure/provenance obstruction story. turn76file2turn76file8turn76file9

## 3) Replace `\label{rem:what-quotient-transport-package-does-and-does-not-prove}`

Replace the **entire remark** with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[What the quotient-transport package does and does not prove]
\label{rem:what-quotient-transport-package-does-and-does-not-prove}
The quotient-transport package now does more than give a single pointwise
scalar compression of the residual exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice.

First,
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-transport-jet-quotient-descent-fixed-shear-corner}
shows that every finite parity-normalized transport jet descends analytically to
the quotient variable
\[
u=t^2.
\]

Second, on the quartic--sextic rung,
Corollary~\ref{cor:rank-one-transport-state-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear}
shows that every finite quotient-visible transport state is locally an analytic
function of the single scalar
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)
\]
alone, and
Corollary~\ref{cor:no-finite-order-hidden-reset-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear}
rules out any third local reset inside that descended state beyond the
involution symmetry \(t\leftrightarrow -t\).

What is \emph{not} proved here is that the actual corrected two-pair defect
package is already state-local in this descended transport state. If that
state-locality held, then
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-state-local-defect-closure-fixed-shear-corner}
would already exclude the residual branch, and under the stronger natural merger
law
Corollary~\ref{cor:stronger-state-local-package-collapse-fixed-shear-corner}
would make the interaction remainder vanish identically.

Accordingly, the present residual mixed burden should now be read as follows:
the exact fixed-shear corner is no longer blocked by a missing local branch
classification or by hidden finite-order transport dynamics. Any remaining
obstruction must come from genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom
structure, or from non-finite-order dependence, not from the descended
transport state alone.
\end{remark}
```

This replaces the older “single scalar + global no-hidden-reset” wording by the stronger finite-state statement that the attack actually proved. turn76file2turn76file9

## 5) Replace `\label{rem:two-point-burden-after-mixed-four-point-closure}`

```latex
\begin{remark}[Two-point burden after mixed four-point closure]
\label{rem:two-point-burden-after-mixed-four-point-closure}
With the clean mixed four-point side now compressed to the scalar exits
\[
T_v=0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\mathcal R=0,
\]
the mixed two-point side should no longer be read as an independent frontier of
mixed local geometry.

The overlap bad set has already split as follows:
\[
(K_v=0,\ S\neq 0)
\]
is absorbed by the mixed low-order obstruction package,
\[
(S=0,\ K_v\neq 0)
\]
is transferred into the established nonmixed \(4\)-point geometry,
and only the exact fixed-shear residual corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
remains genuinely live.

On that residual corner, the quotient-visible transport package is now much
more rigid than a single pointwise scalar. By
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-transport-jet-quotient-descent-fixed-shear-corner},
every finite parity-normalized transport jet descends to the quotient variable

Corollary~\ref{cor:no-finite-order-hidden-reset-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear}
shows that no third local reset survives there.

So the residual exact fixed-shear corner is no longer best viewed as an
unresolved mixed local curvature-branch problem. If the actual corrected
defect/package is state-local in the descended transport state, then the corner
closes by
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-state-local-defect-closure-fixed-shear-corner}
or even by
Corollary~\ref{cor:stronger-state-local-package-collapse-fixed-shear-corner}.

first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom datum that survives
after quotient-visible transport descent, or else from non-finite-order
```

## 6) Replace `\label{rem:residual-mixed-two-point-lane-structural-gain-limitation}`

Replace the **entire remark** with:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Residual mixed two-point lane: structural gain and present limitation]
\label{rem:residual-mixed-two-point-lane-structural-gain-limitation}
The present two-point picture now has three genuine structural gains on the
exact fixed-shear residual corner.

First, after the off-\(K_v=0\) absorption results and the transfer of the
simple-septic-zero slice into the nonmixed \(4\)-point theory, the
derivative-geometric mixed residue is sharply concentrated on the exceptional
corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}.
\]

Second, by
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-transport-jet-quotient-descent-fixed-shear-corner},
every finite parity-normalized transport jet is quotient-visible in the
variable
\[
u=t^2.
\]
So the residual corner is no longer a free two-sided \(t\)-state even at the
finite transport-jet level.

Third, on the quartic--sextic rung,
Corollary~\ref{cor:rank-one-transport-state-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear} shows
that this descended finite transport state has local rank \(1\), and
Corollary~\ref{cor:no-finite-order-hidden-reset-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear}
shows that no finite-order hidden reset survives beyond the involution pair
\(t\leftrightarrow -t\).

What is \emph{not} yet proved is that the actual corrected two-pair defect or
package is already state-local in this descended transport state. If that
state-locality held, then the residual branch would already be excluded by
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-state-local-defect-closure-fixed-shear-corner},
or would collapse identically by
Corollary~\ref{cor:stronger-state-local-package-collapse-fixed-shear-corner}.

Thus the live issue on the mixed residual side is now no longer local
classification and no longer hidden finite-order transport dynamics. It is
whether the first surviving obstruction is already quotient-visible, or instead
comes from genuinely relational / provenance-sensitive two-atom structure or
from non-finite-order dependence.
\end{remark}
```

This is the most direct place to record the “rank-one + no hidden reset + relational obstruction” conclusion. turn76file9

## 7) Optional propagation into `\label{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live}`

If you want the same story reflected in the late global summary, replace the **two-point block** beginning

```latex
the clean algebraic route, ...
```

through the sentence ending

```latex
... no-hidden-reset theorem for the quotient-visible transported overlap
```

with:

```latex
First, on the two-point branch, the exact finite-order source criterion remains
the clean algebraic route, but the naive source-summed corrected block model
cannot prove it: along a weighted one-atom path the extracted finite-order
coefficients are even analytic in the source weight. So the remaining two-point
issue now splits into three conditional lanes: the finite-order source-level
merger route, the weaker quotient-diagonal exact exclusion route, and the exact
projective \(\lambda\)-shear / secant-shadow route on good overlap patches.

In the last route, the overlap bad set is now fully split:
\[
(K_v=0,\ S\neq 0)
\]
is already absorbed by the mixed low-order obstruction package,
\[
(S=0,\ K_v\neq 0)
\]
is already transferred into the established nonmixed \(4\)-point geometry,
and only the exact fixed-shear residual corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
remains genuinely live.

On that residual corner the branch is quotient-diagonal / involutive:
\[
\Phi(t)=\Phi(-t),
\qquad
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u).
\]
Moreover,
Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-transport-jet-quotient-descent-fixed-shear-corner}
shows that every finite parity-normalized transport jet descends to the
quotient variable \(u=t^2\), while
Corollary~\ref{cor:rank-one-transport-state-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear} shows
that on the first live quartic--sextic rung the entire finite quotient-visible
transport state is locally a function of \(Q\) alone. Then
Corollary~\ref{cor:no-finite-order-hidden-reset-quartic-sextic-fixed-shear}
shows that no third local reset survives inside that descended state.

So the residual exact fixed-shear burden is no longer a search for another
local mixed carrier or hidden finite-order transport variable. Rather, it has
become a package-level / provenance-level question: either exact finite-order
merger, or quotient-diagonal continuity/diagonal collapse, or a theorem that
the actual corrected defect/package is already state-local in the descended
transport state. If none of those holds, any still-live obstruction must come
from the first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom input that
survives after quotient-visible transport descent, or from non-finite-order
dependence.
```

This is optional, but it gives the cleanest single-paragraph capture of the whole attack. turn76file1turn76file2turn76file9

## Assistant (2026-04-21 17:15:25)

_Thought for 2m 7s_

I think the new handback lets me push one step further, and it sharpens the residual-corner theorem in a useful way.

The handback already gives the core structural package on the exact fixed-shear residual corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}:
\]
every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to \(u=t^2\), on the quartic–sextic rung the whole finite transport state is locally a function of the single scalar \(Q\), and there is no third local reset beyond the involution \(t\leftrightarrow -t\). It also shows that if the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects are state-local in that descended finite transport state, then the corner is excluded, and if the full two-pair package is state-local with the natural merger law, the interaction remainder dies identically.    

What I think we can now add is this:

the state-local closure theorem extends almost verbatim to **finite analytic relational corrections**.

More precisely, let
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)
\]
be the descended finite transport state along the involutive branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad h(0)=a,\quad h'(0)\neq 0,
\]
and let
\[
R_1(h_1,h_2),\dots,R_M(h_1,h_2)
\]
be finitely many analytic relational scalars such that each \(R_j\) is symmetric,
\[
R_j(h_1,h_2)=R_j(h_2,h_1),
\]
and diagonally normalized,
\[
R_j(h,h)=0.
\]

Then each \(R_j\) is automatically even in the separation variable and divisible by \((h_1-h_2)^2\). In midpoint/separation coordinates
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,
\]
symmetry gives
\[
R_j(m,\delta)=R_j(m,-\delta),
\]
and diagonal normalization gives
\[
R_j(m,0)=0.
\]
So
\[
R_j(m,\delta)=\delta^2 H_j(m,\delta)
\]
for analytic \(H_j\). Along the involutive branch,
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
hence
\[
R_j(h_1(t),h_2(t))=O(t^2).
\]

Now suppose the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects have the form
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)
=
\mathfrak e_3\!\bigl(\mathcal T_N(t),a_1(t),a_2(t),R_1(t),\dots,R_M(t)\bigr),
\]
\[
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)
=
\mathfrak e_5\!\bigl(\mathcal T_N(t),a_1(t),a_2(t),R_1(t),\dots,R_M(t)\bigr),
\]
for analytic functionals \(\mathfrak e_3,\mathfrak e_5\), and assume the diagonal-state normalization
\[
\mathfrak e_3(\mathcal T_N(0),a_1(0),a_2(0),0,\dots,0)=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak e_5(\mathcal T_N(0),a_1(0),a_2(0),0,\dots,0)=0.
\]
Since the descended state satisfies
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathcal T_N(0)+O(t^2)
\]
and each \(R_j(t)=O(t^2)\), analyticity gives
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Therefore
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
and the existing good-patch closeness theorem excludes the branch exactly as in the earlier residual-corner criterion. This uses the same closure mechanism as the handback, but it no longer requires the package to be purely state-local in \(\mathcal T_N\); it allows any **finite symmetric analytic relational correction** that vanishes on the diagonal.   

So the attack now yields a stronger negative finding than before.

A still-live obstruction on the exact fixed-shear residual corner cannot come from

- a second local transport variable on the quartic–sextic rung,
- a third reset inside any finite quotient-visible transport state,
- a state-local two-pair package with the natural merger law,
- or even a package obtained by adding finitely many **symmetric analytic relational variables that vanish on coincidence**.

All of those collapse to \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\) on the involutive branch and are therefore killed by the existing good-patch two-point exclusion mechanism. The only kinds of obstruction left are now much narrower:

1. a relational datum that **does not vanish on coincidence**, so it violates the natural diagonal-merger normalization;
2. a datum that is **not symmetric analytic** in the local pair variables, for example provenance-sensitive or discrete;
3. or genuinely **non-finite-order / nonlocal** dependence. 

That is a real tightening of the frontier.

It means the residual exact fixed-shear corner is now closed under a surprisingly large class of models: anything built from the descended one-atom transport state plus finitely many honest symmetric analytic pair-corrections. So if the corner is still live, the obstruction has to be more exotic than that. In practice, the next thing to attack is therefore not another transport computation, but the first candidate **provenance-sensitive** or **non-diagonally-normalized** two-atom datum that might survive after quotient-visible transport descent.

So my current best sharpened theorem is:

> **Extended conditional closure on the residual exact fixed-shear corner.**  
> If the actual corrected cubic/quintic residual defects are analytic functionals of the descended finite transport state, amplitudes, and finitely many symmetric analytic relational variables vanishing on coincidence, then the residual branch is excluded on every compact good patch.

That is stronger than the original state-local theorem and makes the remaining gap much narrower.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 17:19:13)

_Thought for 2m 42s_

I can push the attack one more step, and I think it materially tightens the residual-corner story.

The handback already gives the fixed-shear involutive package: on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
the branch is quotient-diagonal / involutive, every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to \(u=t^2\), on the quartic–sextic rung the whole finite transport state is locally a function of the single scalar \(Q\), and there is no third local reset beyond \(t\leftrightarrow -t\). It also gives the conditional closure if the defects are state-local in that descended transport state, and the stronger conditional collapse if the full two-pair package is state-local with the natural merger law. 

What I think we can now add is a stronger closure class:

## 1. You do not need pure state-locality; swap-invariant analytic dependence on the amplitude ratio is still harmless

Let
\[
\Lambda(t):=-\frac{a_2(t)}{a_1(t)}
\]
along the involutive branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)).
\]
Under the involution \(t\mapsto -t\), the two atoms swap, so
\[
\Lambda(-t)=\frac{1}{\Lambda(t)}.
\]
This is the natural transformation law for the amplitude ratio.

Now let
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)
\]
be any finite descended transport state. By the handback, on the exact fixed-shear residual corner this state is even:
\[
\mathcal T_N(-t)=\mathcal T_N(t),
\]
and on the quartic–sextic rung it is locally rank \(1\). 

Suppose the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects have the form
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\mathfrak e_3\bigl(\mathcal T_N(t),\Lambda(t),R_1(t),\dots,R_M(t)\bigr),
\]
\[
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\mathfrak e_5\bigl(\mathcal T_N(t),\Lambda(t),R_1(t),\dots,R_M(t)\bigr),
\]
where

- each \(R_j\) is a symmetric analytic relational scalar, so along the involutive branch
  \[
  R_j(-t)=R_j(t),
  \]
- each \(\mathfrak e_j\) is analytic near the diagonal state,
- and each \(\mathfrak e_j\) is **swap-invariant** in the sense
  \[
  \mathfrak e_j(Y,\Lambda,R)=\mathfrak e_j(Y,\Lambda^{-1},R).
  \]

Assume also the diagonal-state normalization
\[
\mathfrak e_3(\mathcal T_N(0),1,R(0))=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak e_5(\mathcal T_N(0),1,R(0))=0.
\]

Then automatically
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(-t)=E_{12}^{(3)}(t),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(-t)=E_{12}^{(5)}(t).
\]
So both defects are even analytic and vanish at \(t=0\), hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
this gives
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
and the existing good-patch closeness corollary excludes the branch exactly as before. This is stronger than the earlier state-local theorem because it allows explicit analytic dependence on the amplitude ratio \(\Lambda\), which need not itself be even or \(O(t^2)\). The involution symmetry kills the linear term for free.

That is a real extension of the closure class.

## 2. The same extension works for any finite symmetric analytic relational corrections

More generally, let
\[
R_1(h_1,h_2,\Lambda),\dots,R_M(h_1,h_2,\Lambda)
\]
be analytic local pair variables satisfying the swap law
\[
R_j(h_1,h_2,\Lambda)=R_j(h_2,h_1,\Lambda^{-1}).
\]
Along the involutive branch this again gives
\[
R_j(-t)=R_j(t).
\]
So any defect built analytically and swap-invariantly from
\[
\mathcal T_N(t),\ \Lambda(t),\ R_1(t),\dots,R_M(t)
\]
is automatically even. If it is normalized to vanish at the diagonal state, it is automatically \(O(t^2)\).

So the residual exact fixed-shear corner is closed under a much broader class of models than “pure state-locality.” It is closed under any **finite analytic swap-invariant model** built from the descended transport state, the amplitude ratio, and finitely many symmetric local relational variables.

This is stronger than what the handback explicitly states.

## 3. What this rules out

Combining this with the handback, a still-live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
cannot come from

- a second local transport variable on the quartic–sextic rung,
- a third local reset inside any finite quotient-visible transport state,
- a state-local two-pair package with the natural merger law,
- or even any finite **analytic swap-invariant** correction built from the descended transport state, the amplitude ratio, and finitely many symmetric local relational variables.

So the only candidates left are now much narrower:

1. a genuinely **non-analytic** dependence on the local cancellation chart,
2. a genuinely **projective/blow-up-direction** dependence that is not analytic at the collision state,
3. a **provenance-sensitive** or discrete two-atom input,
4. or some other genuinely non-finite-order dependence.

That is a substantial tightening of the frontier.

## 4. The likely next target is the blow-up direction

This fits very well with the cancellation-chart insight we already reached. Near a close bad two-point branch on a good patch, the natural variables are
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\mu=\Lambda-1,
\]
and after polar blow-up
\[
(\mu,\delta)=\rho(\cos\theta,\sin\theta),
\]
the first-order cancellation datum is controlled by the projective direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
So if a residual obstruction is still alive after all the analytic swap-invariant closures above, the most plausible place it can hide is not in any ordinary analytic local variable at the collision point, but in the **projective blow-up direction** \(\theta\) itself, or in some provenance-sensitive refinement of that direction.

So the next honest attack is no longer “more transport jets.” It is:

> prove that no swap-invariant dependence on the blown-up cancellation direction can realize a genuine bad branch on a compact good patch.

That now looks like the smallest live theorem still standing.

So the updated handback-quality conclusion is:

the residual exact fixed-shear corner is closed not just under state-local models, but under any finite analytic swap-invariant model built from the descended transport state, the amplitude ratio, and symmetric local pair data. Therefore any remaining obstruction must be genuinely projective/non-analytic/provenance-sensitive.
