## Assistant (2026-04-21 17:21:41)

I’m pushing on the only plausible remaining hideout now: dependence on the blown-up cancellation direction itself. If the residual corner is still live after all the analytic swap-invariant closures, it probably has to come from something singular in the \((\mu,\delta)\)-blow-up rather than from any ordinary local state variable.

_Thought for 2m 1s_

I think the next push gives a genuinely stronger theorem than the state-local version.

The key point is that on the residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
the involution does not just act by \(t\mapsto -t\) on the branch. In the natural cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\Lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
\mu=\Lambda-1,
\]
swapping the two atoms sends
\[
(h_1,h_2,\Lambda)\longmapsto (h_2,h_1,\Lambda^{-1}),
\]
so
\[
\delta\longmapsto -\delta,
\qquad
\mu\longmapsto \frac{1}{1+\mu}-1=-\frac{\mu}{1+\mu}
=-\mu+\mu^2-\mu^3+\cdots.
\]
Call this local involution
\[
\iota(\mu,\delta)=\left(-\frac{\mu}{1+\mu},-\delta\right).
\]

Now take **any** analytic local scalar
\[
F=F(\mu,\delta,Y)
\]
where \(Y\) denotes any finite quotient-visible transport state or any other analytic local variables that are themselves invariant under the involution. If \(F\) is swap-invariant, meaning
\[
F(\mu,\delta,Y)=F(\iota(\mu,\delta),Y),
\]
then along the involutive branch \(t\mapsto -t\) it is automatically even. But more is true: its whole Taylor expansion has no linear part in \((\mu,\delta)\).

Indeed, write
\[
F(\mu,\delta,Y)=F_0(Y)+A(Y)\mu+B(Y)\delta+O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr).
\]
Using \(\iota(\mu,\delta)=(-\mu+O(\mu^2),-\delta)\), swap-invariance forces
\[
A(Y)\mu+B(Y)\delta
=
-A(Y)\mu-B(Y)\delta
\]
to first order, hence
\[
A(Y)=B(Y)=0.
\]
So every analytic swap-invariant local scalar satisfies
\[
F(\mu,\delta,Y)=F_0(Y)+O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr).
\]

This is the useful theorem:

> **Quadratic evenization in the cancellation chart.**  
> Any analytic local scalar on the residual exact fixed-shear corner that is invariant under the atom-swap involution has no first-order term in the cancellation variables \((\mu,\delta)\). If it is normalized so that \(F_0(Y_0)=0\) at the diagonal state, then
> \[
> F=O\!\bigl((|\mu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr).
> \]

Along any analytic involutive branch,
\[
\delta(t)=h(-t)-h(t)=O(t),
\qquad
\mu(t)=\Lambda(t)-1=O(t),
\]
so this gives
\[
F(t)=O(t^2).
\]
And because
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
it follows that
\[
F=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

That means the earlier conditional closure can be widened a lot. You do **not** need pure state-locality in the descended transport state. It is enough that the actual cubic/quintic defects are analytic swap-invariant functions of the local cancellation variables and whatever quotient-visible finite transport state you are using, and that they vanish at the diagonal state. Then the good-patch closeness argument already excludes the branch. This is perfectly consistent with the earlier residual-corner criterion based on evenness and diagonal vanishing, and with the stronger Attack B compression of the transport state to a rank-one quotient-visible package on the quartic–sextic rung. turn82file3turn82file2turn82file14

There is also a second, sharper consequence.

Suppose a would-be obstruction depends only on the **projective blow-up direction**
\[
[\mu:\delta]
\]
near \((\mu,\delta)=(0,0)\). If that dependence extends analytically to the collision state, then it must be trivial. The reason is simple: an analytic function that depends only on direction is homogeneous of degree \(0\), and the only analytic germs with that property are constants. So if such a scalar is also diagonally normalized to vanish at the collision state, it must vanish identically near the origin.

So the attack now yields:

> **Any genuinely live residual obstruction cannot be an analytic function of the projective blow-up direction alone.**

Equivalently, if the corner is still live after all the reductions already proved, the obstruction must be one of the following:

- non-analytic in the cancellation chart \((\mu,\delta)\),
- provenance-sensitive or otherwise not determined by the unordered local pair,
- or non-finite-order / nonlocal.

This is stronger than the earlier “must be relational” statement. It says even a lot of analytic relational dependence is harmless once it respects swap symmetry and diagonal normalization.

So my current best mathematical summary is:

1. the residual exact fixed-shear corner is already quotient-diagonal / involutive; 
2. its finite quotient-visible transport package descends to \(u=t^2\), and on the quartic–sextic rung has local rank \(1\); turn82file2
3. any analytic swap-invariant local defect has no linear term in the cancellation variables \((\mu,\delta)\);
4. therefore any such defect that vanishes at the diagonal state is automatically \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\);
5. so the residual corner is closed under any finite analytic swap-invariant model built from local cancellation variables and the descended transport state;
6. hence any still-live obstruction must be genuinely non-analytic / projective / provenance-sensitive, not just another analytic local scalar.

That is the strongest further push I can currently defend.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 18:34:22)

_Thought for 43s_

I can push it one more step, and this gives a cleaner normal form for the residual corner.

The right local amplitude variable is not \(\mu=\Lambda-1\), but
\[
\nu:=\log \Lambda,
\qquad \Lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
defined near the cancellation point \(\Lambda=1\). On the exact fixed-shear involutive branch, swapping the two atoms sends
\[
\Lambda \longmapsto \Lambda^{-1},
\]
so in the \(\nu\)-coordinate the involution is exactly linear:
\[
\nu \longmapsto -\nu.
\]
At the same time, the separation variable satisfies
\[
\delta:=h_2-h_1 \longmapsto -\delta.
\]
So in the local chart \((\nu,\delta)\), the atom-swap involution is simply
\[
(\nu,\delta)\longmapsto (-\nu,-\delta).
\]

That is much cleaner than working directly with
\[
\mu\longmapsto -\frac{\mu}{1+\mu}.
\]

Now let \(Y\) denote any finite quotient-visible transport state. From the exact fixed-shear analysis, \(Y\) is invariant under the involution, and on the quartic–sextic rung it is locally rank \(1\), controlled by \(Q\). 

Take any analytic local scalar
\[
F=F(\nu,\delta,Y)
\]
that is swap-invariant:
\[
F(\nu,\delta,Y)=F(-\nu,-\delta,Y).
\]
Then \(F\) is an analytic \(\mathbb Z_2\)-invariant germ for the simultaneous sign-flip on \((\nu,\delta)\). The invariant ring is generated by the quadratic monomials
\[
\nu^2,\qquad \nu\delta,\qquad \delta^2.
\]
So there exists an analytic germ \(G\) such that
\[
\boxed{
F(\nu,\delta,Y)=G(\nu^2,\nu\delta,\delta^2,Y).
}
\]

This is stronger than the earlier “no linear term” observation. It says every analytic swap-invariant local scalar factors through the quadratic invariant coordinates. In particular, if
\[
F(0,0,Y_0)=0,
\]
then automatically
\[
F(\nu,\delta,Y)=O\!\bigl(|\nu|^2+|\nu\delta|+|\delta|^2+\|Y-Y_0\|\bigr).
\]

Along an analytic involutive branch,
\[
\delta(t)=O(t),\qquad \nu(t)=\log \Lambda(t)=O(t),\qquad Y(t)=Y(0)+O(t^2),
\]
so
\[
F(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since
\[
h_1-h_2=h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
this gives
\[
F=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

So the residual-corner closure class gets larger again:

if the actual cubic/quintic defects are analytic swap-invariant functions of
\[
(\nu,\delta,Y)
\]
and vanish at the diagonal state, then they are automatically \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and the existing good-patch closeness theorem excludes the branch. This is stronger than the earlier state-local theorem and stronger than the earlier “no linear term in \((\mu,\delta)\)” statement, because it gives an explicit invariant-factorization normal form. 

There is also a sharper negative consequence.

A genuinely live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
cannot come from any analytic scalar that depends only on the local cancellation variables and the descended transport state in a swap-invariant way. Such a scalar always factors through
\[
\nu^2,\ \nu\delta,\ \delta^2,
\]
hence is automatically quadratic at the collision state once normalized to vanish there.

So if the corner is still live, the obstruction must lie beyond that entire analytic invariant world. The remaining possibilities are now very narrow:

- non-analytic dependence on the cancellation chart,
- dependence on the **projective direction**
  \[
  [\nu:\delta]
  \]
  that does not analytically extend through the collision point,
- provenance-sensitive or discrete two-atom data,
- or genuinely nonlocal / non-finite-order dependence.

This also clarifies the blow-up-direction issue. Any dependence on the blown-up direction that is analytic at the collision point is impossible except through the quadratic invariants above. So a truly live “directional” obstruction would have to be singular as \((\nu,\delta)\to(0,0)\); it cannot come from an ordinary analytic local scalar.

So the attack now yields a fairly clean theorem-level statement:

> On the exact fixed-shear residual corner, every analytic swap-invariant local scalar factors through the quadratic invariants \((\nu^2,\nu\delta,\delta^2)\). Hence any such scalar normalized to vanish at the collision state is automatically \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\). Therefore the residual corner is closed under any finite analytic swap-invariant model built from the cancellation variables and the descended transport state.

That is the strongest further reduction I can currently justify. The next live target is no longer “another analytic local variable,” but a genuinely singular or provenance-sensitive dependence on the blown-up direction.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 18:38:58)

I’m pulling the post-update thread into one coherent package now: what was actually proved, what was reduced, and what remains genuinely open.

_Thought for 33s_

Here is the complete math-form handback for everything I found **since the last paper update** on the \(2\)-point attack.

## 1. The live \(2\)-point routes are now sharply separated

There are still three conditional \(2\)-point routes.

First, the **strong finite-order source-level route**: prove the actual corrected two-pair cubic/quintic/septic package satisfies the finite-order merger criterion on small two-atom data. Second, the **weaker exact quotient-diagonal route**: construct the actual corrected two-atom quotient germ with continuity and exact diagonal collapse. Third, the **mixed \(\lambda\)-shear / projective-shadow route** on a good overlap patch. What is no longer viable is the naive source-summed corrected-block route: the even-amplitude audit shows it cannot supply the linear merger law.  

## 2. The overlap geometry is now fully split

On a good overlap patch, any close exact mixed \(2\)-point bad branch can accumulate only on
\[
\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}.
\]
Inside the additional exact fixed-shear overlap lane, this has now sharpened to the trichotomy:
\[
(K_v=0,\ S\neq 0)\quad\text{mixed low-order,}
\]
\[
(S=0,\ K_v\neq 0)\quad\text{transfers to nonmixed \(4\)-point,}
\]
and only
\[
\boxed{\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}}
\]
remains as the genuinely residual derivative-geometric corner. This is one of the main structural gains of the attack.  turn83file14

## 3. The residual exact fixed-shear corner is quotient-diagonal / involutive

On the residual exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice, after centering and analytic source reparametrization, the projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad
m\ \text{even},\quad G(-t)=G(t).
\]
Hence
\[
\Phi(t)=\Phi(-t),
\]
and the local branch descends to the quotient variable
\[
u=t^2,
\qquad
\Phi(t)=\widehat\Phi(u).
\]
So the residual local exact repeated-value branch is not a free two-point branch anymore; it is the pullback of a quotient-diagonal branch. turn83file14

## 4. Quotient transport scalar and even-support residual ladder

The key regularized ratio is
\[
Q(t):=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)},
\]
and on the involutive branch it is even:
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Writing
\[
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}
=
2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\]
and
\[
e:=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D},\qquad
r:=\ord_0J_\lambda=\ord_0K_v,
\]
one gets the residual ladder
\[
q-r=2e+2,
\qquad
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=r+2e+4,
\]
together with
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
\]
So the residual exact fixed-shear lane lives on an **even-support ladder** over \(K_v=0\), while the source Wronskian still vanishes to odd order. turn83file11turn83file14

## 5. Quartic–sextic rung: local quotient injectivity and no re-entry

At the first surviving rung
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0),
\]
the current package implies
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0.
\]
So \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in the quotient variable \(u=t^2\). Equivalently, there is no local exact fixed-shear re-entry after quotienting the involution on this quartic–sextic residual rung. This is a genuine no-go theorem, even though by itself it is not yet a full closure theorem. turn83file4turn83file13

## 6. Finite transport-jet quotient descent

A major upgrade over the earlier “one even scalar” picture is that the entire finite transport-jet package descends. Define parity-normalized transport jets
\[
\Theta_k(t):=t^{-(k\bmod 2)}Q^{(k)}(t),
\qquad k\ge 0.
\]
Because \(Q\) is even, each \(\Theta_k\) is again even analytic, so each has the form
\[
\Theta_k(t)=\widetilde\Theta_k(t^2)
\]
for a unique analytic quotient germ \(\widetilde\Theta_k\). In particular,
\[
X(t):=\frac{Q'(t)}{t}
\]
is even analytic and equals
\[
X(t)=2\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
So every finite parity-normalized transport jet is quotient-visible. turn83file0

## 7. Rank-one transport-state theorem on the quartic–sextic rung

On the quartic–sextic rung, \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in \(u\). Therefore every descended transport jet \(\widetilde\Theta_k(u)\) can be re-expressed as an analytic function of \(\widehat Q(u)\), hence of \(Q(t)\) itself:
\[
\Theta_k(t)=F_k(Q(t)).
\]
So for any finite transport state
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t)),
\]
there exists an analytic map \(\mathbf F_N\) with
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathbf F_N(Q(t)).
\]
This is the **rank-one transport-state theorem**: on the first live residual rung, the whole finite quotient-visible transport state is locally controlled by the single scalar \(Q\). There is no hidden second finite transport variable. turn83file2

## 8. No finite-order hidden reset

From the rank-one statement one gets:
\[
\mathcal T_N(t_1)=\mathcal T_N(t_2)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
Q(t_1)=Q(t_2).
\]
But \(Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)\) and \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective in \(u\), so
\[
t_2=\pm t_1.
\]
Thus no finite quotient-visible transport state can produce a third local reset beyond the involution symmetry \(t\leftrightarrow -t\). This rules out an entire class of hidden-state explanations for a still-live residual corner. turn83file2

## 9. Residual-corner closure if the actual defects are finite-state-local

Let
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)
\]
be a finite descended transport state along the involutive branch. If the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\mathfrak e_3(\mathcal T_N(t),a_1(t),a_2(t)),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\mathfrak e_5(\mathcal T_N(t),a_1(t),a_2(t)),
\]
for analytic functionals \(\mathfrak e_3,\mathfrak e_5\), and vanish on the diagonal state, then
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathcal T_N(0)+O(t^2),
\]
hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Because
\[
h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
this becomes
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},\ E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\]
which is exactly the scale needed for the already-proved defect-closeness exclusion mechanism on a compact good patch. So under this state-locality hypothesis, the residual branch is excluded. turn83file13

## 10. Stronger conditional collapse if the full two-pair package is state-local with merger law

A stronger conditional statement also holds. Suppose the corrected two-pair package is built from the two individual finite transport states,
\[
\mathcal P_2(t)
=
\mathfrak P_2\bigl(a_1(t),a_2(t);\mathcal T_N(h_1(t)),\mathcal T_N(h_2(t))\bigr),
\]
and satisfies the natural diagonal merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y,Y)=(a_1+a_2)\mathfrak F(Y),
\]
where \(\mathfrak F(Y)\) is the corresponding one-atom package. Along the involutive branch, each \(\Theta_k\) is even, so
\[
\mathcal T_N(h_1(t))=\mathcal T_N(h_2(t)).
\]
Hence the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(t):=
\mathcal P_2(t)-a_1(t)F_{h_1(t)}-a_2(t)F_{h_2(t)}
\]
must vanish identically:
\[
\mathcal I_2(t)\equiv 0.
\]
So under this stronger hypothesis the corner does not merely satisfy a quadratic smallness estimate; the interaction part dies identically on the involutive branch. 

## 11. Central negative finding from Attack B

If the exact fixed-shear residual corner is still genuinely live, then the obstruction cannot come from any hidden finite-order behavior inside the quotient-visible transport jet itself. More concretely, it cannot come from:

- a second local transport variable on the quartic–sextic rung,
- a third reset inside any finite parity-normalized transport state,
- or a two-pair model built only from the two separate quotient-visible one-atom states, assuming the natural merger law.

So any still-live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
must come from something beyond that descended transport package: genuinely relational two-atom data, provenance-sensitive input, or non-finite-order dependence. This is the central negative result of the attack. turn83file12

## 12. Correction to the old diagonal picture: the right local chart is the collision-cancellation chart

A further refinement is that the relevant “collision” chart for close bad two-point cores on a good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\) is not the raw diagonal with arbitrary total amplitude, but the **cancellation chart**
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
\mu=\lambda-1.
\]
Indeed, the cubic identity forces \(\lambda\to 1\) as \(\delta\to 0\) on \(J\). The best local replacement for the old quadratic-factorization target is then a **blown-up cubic/quintic limit theorem** at the collision-cancellation locus. After projectivization, the effective first-order source direction is
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m',
\]
and the right theorem to aim at is that the corrected cubic/quintic witness depends only on this blown-up projective source direction. That fits the even-amplitude obstruction and the scale cancellation in whitening, and it matches the actual limiting geometry of close bad two-point cores. 

## 13. Extended closure class: finite analytic relational corrections are still harmless

The residual-corner closure theorem can be widened beyond pure state-locality. If the actual corrected defects depend analytically on the descended transport state together with finitely many symmetric analytic relational scalars
\[
R_j(h_1,h_2)
\]
satisfying
\[
R_j(h_1,h_2)=R_j(h_2,h_1),
\qquad
R_j(h,h)=0,
\]
then along the involutive branch each \(R_j\) is even and in fact
\[
R_j=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
So any defect built analytically from \(\mathcal T_N\) and finitely many such diagonally normalized symmetric relational corrections is still \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), hence excluded by the same good-patch mechanism. Thus a still-live obstruction cannot come from any **finite symmetric analytic relational correction** of that type. This tightens the frontier further. (This is an inference from combining the involutive geometry with the closure mechanism above.) turn83file13

## 14. Swap-invariant analytic dependence on the amplitude ratio is also harmless

One can go further. Along the involutive branch,
\[
\Lambda(t):=-\frac{a_2(t)}{a_1(t)}
\]
transforms under swap by
\[
\Lambda(-t)=\Lambda(t)^{-1}.
\]
So if the actual defects are analytic **swap-invariant** functions of the descended transport state, the amplitude ratio \(\Lambda\), and finitely many symmetric local relational variables, then they are automatically even in \(t\). If they vanish at the diagonal state, they are again \(O(t^2)\), hence \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\). So the residual corner is closed under any finite analytic **swap-invariant** model built from the descended transport state, the amplitude ratio, and symmetric local pair data. This rules out a much broader class of candidate obstructions than the original state-local theorem alone. (Again, this is a derived consequence of the involution structure plus the existing residual-corner criterion.) turn83file12

## 15. Strongest local invariant normal form: the \(\nu=\log\Lambda\) chart

The cleanest local amplitude variable is
\[
\nu:=\log\Lambda,
\]
defined near \(\Lambda=1\). Then under atom swap,
\[
\nu\mapsto -\nu,
\qquad
\delta\mapsto -\delta.
\]
So in the chart \((\nu,\delta)\), the involution is simply
\[
(\nu,\delta)\mapsto(-\nu,-\delta).
\]
For any analytic swap-invariant local scalar
\[
F=F(\nu,\delta,Y),
\]
where \(Y\) is any involution-invariant finite transport state, invariant theory gives the normal form
\[
F(\nu,\delta,Y)=G(\nu^2,\nu\delta,\delta^2,Y)
\]
for an analytic germ \(G\). So every analytic swap-invariant local scalar factors through the quadratic invariants
\[
\nu^2,\qquad \nu\delta,\qquad \delta^2.
\]
If it vanishes at the diagonal state, it is automatically \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\). This is the strongest local normal-form statement obtained in the attack. It shows that any genuinely live residual obstruction cannot come from an ordinary analytic swap-invariant local scalar at all. (This is a mathematical consequence of the involution linearization in the \((\nu,\delta)\) chart.) turn83file12

## 16. Final negative finding: what kinds of obstruction are still logically possible

Putting everything together, a still-live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
cannot come from any of the following:

- hidden finite-order behavior inside the quotient-visible transport state,
- a second transport variable on the quartic–sextic rung,
- a third local reset,
- a state-local two-pair package with the natural merger law,
- a finite symmetric analytic relational correction,
- or even any finite analytic swap-invariant local scalar built from the cancellation variables, amplitude ratio, and descended transport state.

So if the corner is still live, the obstruction must be genuinely more exotic: non-analytic in the cancellation chart, projective/blow-up-direction dependent without analytic extension through the collision point, provenance-sensitive/discrete, or non-finite-order / nonlocal. This is the strongest “what remains” theorem-level conclusion I have from the attack. turn83file12

## 17. Septic quotient defect: where it still matters and how it was reduced

For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, the local exclusion theorem only needs the cubic and quintic defects via the already-proved good-patch closeness estimate, so the septic quotient defect is not part of that local contradiction. But for the **stronger global source-level merger route**, the septic rung still matters because the tracked package is
\[
\mathbf C\oplus \mathfrak f\oplus \bigl(\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\bigr).
\]
There the order-\(7\) target is only the quotient statement
\[
A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1,h;a_2,h)-A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}(a_1+a_2,h)
\in \mathbf C\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]
equivalently vanishing of the septic quotient defect. Formally, once two corrected germs agree through cubic and quintic order and differ only by odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower scalar/value gauge, the order-\(7\) mismatch is automatically a multiple of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\). The real remaining theorem there is therefore not “prove full order-\(7\) equality,” but prove same reduced image germ or collision-functoriality of the corrected-block construction on the collision/cancellation locus. L1462-L1480

## Bottom line

The strongest honest summary is this.

The residual exact fixed-shear corner is now much more rigid than before. It is quotient-diagonal / involutive; the whole finite transport package is quotient-visible; on the first live quartic–sextic rung it has local rank \(1\); no hidden finite-order reset survives there; and any finite analytic swap-invariant local scalar vanishing at the diagonal state is automatically quadratic in the branch parameter and therefore harmless. So the \(2\)-point problem is no longer blocked by generic local geometry. The remaining burden is package-level and genuinely relational/provenance-sensitive: either prove the finite-order source-level merger theorem, or the weaker exact quotient-diagonal theorem, or show that no genuinely non-analytic / provenance-sensitive two-atom datum survives after quotient-visible transport descent.

with

then on a good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), cubic cancellation picks a unique projective direction and the quintic witness is nonzero there because it evaluates to \(-M(m)\). So close cancelling bad two-point cores are excluded locally on such a patch. That is an excellent sharpening of the local target.

For the **residual exact fixed-shear corner**, the new updates reinforce that cubic/quintic control is the natural first local target; septic is not the first live local obstruction on a good patch. \]
is still the honest order-\(7\) obstruction after lower universal structure is quotiented out. So my previous split still stands: cubic/quintic are the right local blown-up target on good patches, while septic remains important for the stronger global coincidence/functoriality route. 

So my integrated verdict is:

The other two chats’ updates make the \(2\)-point picture more coherent. They support the claim that the universal transport geometry is essentially exhausted on the residual exact fixed-shear corner, and they sharpen the best next local theorem from “some residual-corner closure criterion” into a much cleaner target: prove **blown-up cubic/quintic functoriality** in the collision-cancellation chart. If that lands, close cancelling bad two-point cores are gone on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\). ## Assistant (2026-04-21 19:41:10)

_Thought for 9s_

I think the clean next push is this:

the local \(2\)-point theorem on a good patch does **not** need exact blown-up functoriality. It is enough to prove a **stable perturbative version** of it.

Here is the idea.

Work in the collision-cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
\omega:=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1},
\]
so swap acts by
\[
(m,\omega,\delta)\mapsto(m,-\omega,-\delta).
\]
The other handback already shows that for any swap-even analytic corrected defect with collision vanishing, the whole linear blown-up layer is dead and one gets the exact factorization
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta},
\]
with \(\mathcal H\) analytic, and on the involutive branch even this quadratic coefficient is quotient-visible; on the quartic–sextic rung it is a function of \(Q\) alone. 

So the real local objects to study are the **quadratic coefficients**
\[
H_3(m,\kappa):=\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0),
\qquad
H_5(m,\kappa):=\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0).
\]

The previous handback proposed the exact one-pair blow-up laws
\[
H_3(m,\kappa)=C(m,\kappa):=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\]
\[
H_5(m,\kappa)=K(m,\kappa):=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
up to the harmless normalization convention on \(\kappa\). In that notation, cubic cancellation picks the unique slope
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\,\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)},
\]
and then
\[
K(m,\kappa_*(m))
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)},
\]
so on a good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
this is uniformly nonzero. That is the exact cubic/quintic exclusion mechanism already identified in the other handback. 

What I think is new is that you do not need those formulas **exactly**. A robust perturbative theorem is enough.

Assume the corrected cubic/quintic defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\Bigl(C(m,\kappa)+R_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2)\Bigr),
\]
\[
E_{12}^{(5)}(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\Bigl(K(m,\kappa)+R_5(m,\kappa,\delta^2)\Bigr),
\]
where \(R_3,R_5\) are continuous in \((m,\kappa,\delta^2)\), analytic in the local variables, and
\[
R_3(m,\kappa,0)=R_5(m,\kappa,0)=0.
\]

Then on any compact good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), there is an \(\varepsilon_J>0\) such that for sufficiently small \(|\delta|\), the equations
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}=0
\]
have no nontrivial solution with \(m\in J\).

The proof is simple and I think it is the right next theorem.

Because \(c\neq 0\) on \(J\), the cubic model
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m)
\]
has a unique zero
\[
\kappa=\kappa_*(m)=2\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
Moreover
\[
\partial_\kappa C(m,\kappa)=-\frac12 c(m),
\]
so on compact \(J\) this derivative is uniformly bounded away from zero. Hence by the implicit function theorem, for sufficiently small \(|\delta|\) the perturbed cubic equation
\[
C(m,\kappa)+R_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2)=0
\]
still has a unique solution
\[
\kappa=\kappa_\delta(m)
\]
with
\[
\kappa_\delta(m)=\kappa_*(m)+O(\delta^2),
\]
uniformly on \(J\).

Now evaluate the quintic coefficient there:
\[
K(m,\kappa_\delta(m))+R_5(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2).
\]
Since
\[
K(m,\kappa_*(m))=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)},
\]
and \(M/c\) is uniformly bounded away from zero on compact \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), continuity gives
\[
K(m,\kappa_\delta(m))+R_5(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2)\neq 0
\]
for all sufficiently small \(|\delta|\). So cubic and quintic cannot vanish simultaneously.

That gives a robust local exclusion theorem:

> **Stable blown-up cubic/quintic exclusion on good patches.**  
> If the corrected cubic/quintic defects admit swap-even collision-chart factorizations whose quadratic coefficients are perturbations of the model pair \((C,K)\) vanishing at \(\delta=0\), then there are no close cancelling bad two-point cores on any compact good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\).

This is stronger than asking for exact functoriality and, I think, much more plausible to prove from the actual corrected package. It only asks that the leading quadratic blown-up law stabilize to the one-pair model at \(\delta=0\).  

There is an even cleaner formulation.

Instead of proving exact asymptotics
\[
\mathcal C_3=\rho\,C+o(\rho),\qquad \mathcal C_5=\rho\,K+o(\rho),
\]
one can aim to prove the weaker but sufficient **quadratic coefficient convergence**
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2)\to C(m,\kappa),
\qquad
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,\delta^2)\to K(m,\kappa)
\]
uniformly on compact sets as \(\delta\to 0\). Since the whole linear blown-up layer is already killed by symmetry, this is the real coefficient-level theorem needed locally. The quartic–sextic rank-one transport result suggests that, on the residual exact fixed-shear corner, any still-live deviation from this model has to come from genuinely package-level relational data, not from hidden universal transport structure. 

So the attack now reduces the best local theorem target to:

1. prove swap-even analyticity in the collision-cancellation chart;
2. extract the quadratic coefficients \(\mathcal H_3,\mathcal H_5\);
3. show they converge to the one-pair model pair \((C,K)\) as \(\delta\to 0\);
4. conclude local exclusion on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) by the stable transversality argument above.

That is, to my mind, the cleanest next \(2\)-point theorem still standing. It is more realistic than exact package functoriality, and sharper than the previous general “state-local” closure.

I’m pushing on the stable local theorem now, not the exact functoriality version. The question is whether a hypothetical bad branch would force a perturbed cubic-killing slope \(\kappa_\delta(m)\), and whether the quintic coefficient can stay uniformly away from zero there.

_Thought for 12s_

Here is the next push, and I think it gives the sharpest **local contradiction scheme** so far.

The right object is no longer the raw defects \(E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}\) themselves, but their **quadratic coefficients** in the collision-cancellation chart. The other chat already showed that any analytic swap-even corrected defect with collision vanishing has the exact form
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta},
\]
and that on the involutive residual exact fixed-shear branch this becomes
\[
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\widetilde H(t^2).
\]
So the whole linear blown-up layer is dead, and the first surviving transverse layer is encoded by the coefficient germ \(\mathcal H\). 

Let me write
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,\delta^2).
\]
The best local theorem target is now:

\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2)\to C(m,\kappa),
\qquad
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,\delta^2)\to K(m,\kappa)
\]
uniformly on compact sets as \(\delta\to 0\), where
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\qquad
K(m,\kappa)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
That is weaker than exact blown-up functoriality, but it is enough for exclusion on any compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\qquad
M=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c' A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
This uses exactly the good-patch determinant structure from the other handback. 

The clean argument is this.

Because \(c\neq 0\) on \(J\), the model cubic coefficient
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m)
\]
has a unique zero
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\,\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
Also
\[
\partial_\kappa C(m,\kappa)=-\frac12 c(m),
\]
so on compact \(J\) this derivative is uniformly bounded away from zero. Therefore, if \(\mathcal H_3\) is uniformly close to \(C\), then for sufficiently small \(|\delta|\) the perturbed cubic equation
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2)=0
\]
has a unique solution
\[
\kappa=\kappa_\delta(m)
\]
near \(\kappa_*(m)\), with
\[
\kappa_\delta(m)=\kappa_*(m)+O(\delta^2)
\]
uniformly on \(J\). This is just the uniform implicit function theorem. So any putative close bad branch is forced onto a unique perturbed cubic-killing slope. 

Now evaluate the quintic coefficient there:
\[
\mathcal H_5\bigl(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2\bigr).
\]
At the model slope,
\[
K\bigl(m,\kappa_*(m)\bigr)
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
Since \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), the quotient \(M/c\) is uniformly bounded away from zero on \(J\). So if \(\mathcal H_5\) is uniformly close to \(K\) and \(\kappa_\delta(m)\) stays close to \(\kappa_*(m)\), then
\[
\mathcal H_5\bigl(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2\bigr)\neq 0
\]
for all sufficiently small \(|\delta|\). In other words, the quintic coefficient cannot vanish at the perturbed cubic-killing slope. So
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}=0
\]
cannot hold simultaneously for sufficiently close cancelling configurations on \(J\). That excludes close bad two-point cores locally on good patches. 

So the strongest local theorem I can now defend is:

> **Stable blown-up cubic/quintic exclusion on good patches.**  
> Assume the corrected cubic/quintic defects are analytic swap-even functions in the collision-cancellation chart, with exact quadratic factorizations
> \[
> E_{12}^{(j)}=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,\delta^2),\qquad j=3,5,
> \]
> and assume
> \[
> \mathcal H_3\to C,\qquad \mathcal H_5\to K
> \]
> uniformly on compact sets as \(\delta\to 0\). Then on every compact good patch
> \[
> J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
> \]
> there are no sufficiently close cancelling bad two-point cores.

This is materially weaker than exact functoriality and seems much more plausible to extract from the actual corrected package. It uses only:

1. swap-even analyticity in the correct cancellation chart;
2. the exact quadratic factorization already forced by symmetry;
3. convergence of the quadratic coefficients to the one-pair model pair \((C,K)\).

Everything else is robust transversality. turn84file1

There is one more useful sharpening.

Because the quartic–sextic residual corner already has rank-one quotient-visible transport state, if a residual obstruction still survives after this theorem, it cannot come from any ordinary perturbation of the model pair \((C,K)\) by universal transport data alone. It would have to enter through the first genuinely **package-level relational correction** to the quadratic coefficients
\[
\mathcal H_3,\qquad \mathcal H_5.
\]
So the next mathematical target is not “another local geometry theorem,” but to identify the first possible relational correction term in the quadratic coefficient normal form and ask whether it can change the sign gap at the cubic-killing slope. That is now the smallest live local question I see.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 19:45:11)

_Thought for 48s_

I think I can push the local theorem one rung further, and it improves the target materially.

The key point is that for local exclusion on a good patch, you do **not** need full uniform convergence of the quadratic coefficients on compact \((m,\kappa)\)-sets. It is enough to know their **edge values at \(\delta=0\)**.

Let me write the exact quadratic factorizations in the collision-cancellation chart as
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta}.
\]
This exact factorization is already forced by swap-even analyticity and collision vanishing, and on the involutive residual corner the whole quadratic layer is quotient-visible. 

The model pair coming from the one-pair linearization is
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\qquad
K(m,\kappa)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
and on a good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\qquad
M=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c' A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
the unique model cubic-killing slope is
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\,\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)},
\]
with
\[
K(m,\kappa_*(m))
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}\neq 0.
\]
That is the determinant mechanism already isolated in the other handback. 

Now here is the stronger local theorem target.

Assume only the **edge identities**
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=C(m,\kappa),
\qquad
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=K(m,\kappa).
}
\]
Because \(\mathcal H_3,\mathcal H_5\) are analytic in \((m,\kappa,\delta^2)\), that already implies the stable exclusion theorem.

The reason is analytic perturbation theory. Since
\[
\partial_\kappa C(m,\kappa)=-\frac12 c(m),
\]
and \(c\neq 0\) on \(J\), the equation
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,\delta^2)=0
\]
has, for sufficiently small \(|\delta|\), a unique analytic solution
\[
\kappa=\kappa_\delta(m)
\]
near \(\kappa_*(m)\), with
\[
\kappa_\delta(m)=\kappa_*(m)+O(\delta^2)
\]
uniformly on \(J\). This is just the analytic implicit function theorem applied at \(\delta^2=0\).

Then define the reduced quintic obstruction along the perturbed cubic-killing graph:
\[
\mathfrak R(m,\delta^2):=
\mathcal H_5\bigl(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2\bigr).
\]
Since everything is analytic, \(\mathfrak R\) is analytic in \((m,\delta^2)\), and at \(\delta=0\),
\[
\mathfrak R(m,0)=K(m,\kappa_*(m))=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
Because \(M/c\) is uniformly bounded away from \(0\) on compact \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), continuity gives
\[
\mathfrak R(m,\delta^2)\neq 0
\]
for all sufficiently small \(|\delta|\), uniformly in \(m\in J\). Therefore the system
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}=0
\]
has no nontrivial close solutions on \(J\).

So the theorem becomes:

> **Edge-value local exclusion theorem.**  
> If the corrected cubic/quintic defects admit swap-even collision-chart factorizations
> \[
> E_{12}^{(j)}=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,\delta^2),\qquad j=3,5,
> \]
> and their edge values at \(\delta=0\) coincide with the one-pair model pair
> \[
> \mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=C(m,\kappa),\qquad
> \mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=K(m,\kappa),
> \]
> then there are no sufficiently close cancelling bad two-point cores on any compact good patch
> \[
> J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
> \]

This is better than the previous target. Before, I was asking for uniform convergence
\[
\mathcal H_3\to C,\qquad \mathcal H_5\to K
\]
as \(\delta\to 0\). But analyticity already gives that once the edge identities are known. So the **real local theorem** to prove is only the boundary-value statement at \(\delta=0\), not a full convergence theorem. turn84file1

That reduces the local attack to something much more concrete:

1. prove swap-even analyticity in the collision-cancellation chart;
2. extract the exact quadratic coefficients \(\mathcal H_3,\mathcal H_5\);
3. prove only their **edge values** at \(\delta=0\) equal the one-pair model pair \((C,K)\).

Once those three things are in hand, the local exclusion on good patches is formal.

There is also a cleaner way to phrase the last remaining local obstruction. It is no longer “some residual bad branch.” It is the reduced scalar
\[
\mathfrak R(m,\delta^2)=\mathcal H_5\bigl(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2\bigr),
\]
the quintic coefficient evaluated on the unique perturbed cubic-killing graph. A close bad branch exists only if
\[
\mathfrak R(m,\delta^2)=0.
\]
But the edge identity gives
\[
\mathfrak R(m,0)=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
So the entire local problem on a good patch has been compressed to showing that the actual corrected package has the right **edge value**
\[
\mathfrak R(m,0)=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]

That, to me, is the cleanest next theorem still standing. It is smaller than exact blown-up functoriality, smaller than full source-level merger, and exactly targeted to the local cancellation geometry.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 19:46:43)

_Thought for 31s_

I think the attack now reduces one rung further, and this is the cleanest local theorem target so far.

The last step already showed that on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
local exclusion does **not** need full blown-up functoriality. It is enough to know the edge identities
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=C(m,\kappa),\qquad
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=K(m,\kappa),
\]
for the quadratic coefficients in the collision-cancellation chart. Once those hold, analyticity gives the perturbed cubic-killing graph \(\kappa_\delta(m)\), and the reduced quintic obstruction
\[
\mathfrak R(m,\delta^2)
:=
\mathcal H_5\bigl(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2\bigr)
\]
satisfies
\[
\mathfrak R(m,0)=K(m,\kappa_*(m))=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)},
\]
so \(\mathfrak R\neq 0\) for sufficiently small \(|\delta|\) on \(J\), excluding close bad two-point cores.  

So the real question is now:

**why should the edge values \(\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0),\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)\) equal the one-pair model pair \((C,K)\)?**

I think the answer is that this is really a **first-variation theorem** in the cancellation direction.

## 1. The edge \(\delta=0\) is a directional linearization problem

In the cancellation chart,
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
\omega=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1},
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta},
\]
and the other handback already identified the correct first-order source direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m',
\]
or, in the \((m,\kappa,\delta)\)-normalization, the equivalent affine form
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\delta\Bigl(D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m\Bigr)+O(\delta^2),
\]
up to the fixed sign/normalization convention for \(\kappa\). This is exactly why the model pair has the form
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\qquad
K(m,\kappa)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
These are simply the directional derivatives of the one-pair cubic/quintic data in the cancellation direction. 

So the edge-value theorem is really this:

> **Directional first-variation theorem at cancellation.**  
> The first nonzero blown-up coefficient of the corrected cubic/quintic defect is the directional derivative of the one-pair cubic/quintic witness along the first-order cancellation direction
> \[
> V_\kappa:=\partial_h-\frac{\kappa}{2}\,\mathrm{Id},
> \]
> namely
> \[
> \mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=V_\kappa c(m),
> \qquad
> \mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=V_\kappa A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
> \]

That is the sharp local theorem to attack.

## 2. Why this is enough

Once that directional theorem holds, the whole local exclusion is formal.

Indeed,
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m)
\]
has unique zero
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}
\]
on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), because
\[
\partial_\kappa \mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=-\frac12 c(m)
\]
is uniformly bounded away from \(0\). Then
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa_*(m),0)
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
So on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), this is uniformly nonzero. By analytic perturbation in \(\delta^2\), the perturbed cubic-killing graph \(\kappa_\delta(m)\) persists and the reduced quintic obstruction stays nonzero for small \(|\delta|\). Therefore
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}=0
\]
cannot hold simultaneously for sufficiently close cancelling configurations. That is exactly the stable local exclusion theorem. 

So the whole local problem is now compressed to proving the **edge directional derivative identities**, not full functoriality.

## 3. What is strictly weaker than blown-up functoriality

This is an important refinement.

Earlier, the natural target was something like exact blown-up functoriality:
\[
\mathcal C_3(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,C(m,\theta)+o(\rho),
\qquad
\mathcal C_5(m,\rho,\theta)=\rho\,K(m,\theta)+o(\rho).
\]
That is stronger than what we now need.

Because swap-evenness already kills the entire linear blown-up layer and forces exact quadratic factorization
\[
E_{12}^{(j)}=\delta^2\,\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad j=3,5,
\]
the only thing needed locally is the **boundary value**
\[
\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0).
\]
So the best theorem target is not full asymptotic functoriality in \((\rho,\theta)\); it is just:

> identify the quadratic edge coefficients at \(\delta=0\) with the directional derivatives of the one-pair model.

That is materially smaller.

## 4. A clean normal form for the remaining local obstruction

This also gives a better formulation of the only remaining local obstruction.

Define the unique perturbed cubic-killing graph \(\kappa_\delta(m)\) by
\[
\mathcal H_3\bigl(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2\bigr)=0.
\]
Then the whole local two-point problem on a good patch is encoded by the single scalar
\[
\mathfrak R(m,\delta^2):=
\mathcal H_5\bigl(m,\kappa_\delta(m),\delta^2\bigr).
\]
A close bad branch exists only if
\[
\mathfrak R(m,\delta^2)=0.
\]
But the edge-value theorem would give
\[
\mathfrak R(m,0)=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
So on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), the entire local problem reduces to showing that the actual corrected package has the correct **edge value**
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R(m,0)=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
}
\]

That is the smallest honest local theorem I see now.

## 5. What this says about where a failure could still hide

If the local exclusion theorem still fails after all this, then the failure cannot be in generic analytic dependence on the cancellation chart. It has to be in one of two places:

either the actual corrected package fails the directional first-variation identities
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=C(m,\kappa),\qquad
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=K(m,\kappa),
\]
or the first genuinely relational/package-level correction already changes the edge value \(\mathfrak R(m,0)\).

In other words, the frontier is now even narrower:
the issue is not “does some bad branch exist?” but “does the corrected package have the expected first variation at the cancellation edge?”

That is a much cleaner attack target than any earlier formulation.

## 6. The best next theorem to prove

So my next concrete theorem target is:

> **Cancellation-edge first-variation theorem.**  
> In the collision-cancellation chart, the quadratic coefficients of the corrected cubic/quintic defects satisfy
> \[
> \mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
> \]
> \[
> \mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
> \]

If that theorem lands, then close cancelling bad two-point cores are excluded locally on every compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]

That is the sharpest local theorem still standing, and it is significantly smaller than exact blown-up functoriality or the full strong source-level merger theorem.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 19:50:01)

_Thought for 1m 59s_

I can push the local attack one rung further, and this is the cleanest reduction I have so far.

The key observation is that once you pass to the **linearized swap chart**
\[
\nu:=\log\lambda,\qquad \delta:=h_2-h_1,
\]
the atom-swap involution is exactly
\[
(\nu,\delta)\longmapsto(-\nu,-\delta).
\]
So any analytic swap-invariant corrected defect is an analytic \(\mathbb Z_2\)-invariant germ in \((\nu,\delta)\).

That means the first surviving local information is completely encoded by its **quadratic jet**.

Let \(E_j\) denote either corrected defect, \(j=3,5\). Then after fixing the midpoint \(m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2}\), any analytic swap-invariant local representative has the form
\[
E_j(m,\nu,\delta)
=
A_j(m)\nu^2+B_j(m)\nu\delta+C_j(m)\delta^2
+
O\!\bigl((|\nu|+|\delta|)^4\bigr).
\]
There are no linear terms, and there are exactly three quadratic coefficients.

Now along a cancellation slope
\[
\nu=\kappa\,\delta+O(\delta^3),
\]
one gets
\[
E_j(m,\nu,\delta)
=
\delta^2\Bigl(A_j(m)\kappa^2+B_j(m)\kappa+C_j(m)\Bigr)
+
O(\delta^4).
\]
So the edge coefficient in the collision-cancellation chart is not an arbitrary function at all: it is **automatically a quadratic polynomial in \(\kappa\)**:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0)=A_j(m)\kappa^2+B_j(m)\kappa+C_j(m).
}
\]

That is a real reduction. The whole local theorem target has now collapsed to identifying the three coefficients
\[
A_j(m),\qquad B_j(m),\qquad C_j(m)
\]
for \(j=3,5\).

For the model pair coming from the one-pair directional law,
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\qquad
K(m,\kappa)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
this means the desired edge identities are exactly
\[
A_3(m)=0,\qquad B_3(m)=-\frac12 c(m),\qquad C_3(m)=c'(m),
\]
\[
A_5(m)=0,\qquad B_5(m)=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),\qquad C_5(m)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m).
\]

So the strong local exclusion theorem on a good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\qquad
M=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c' A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
has now been reduced to these **six scalar jet identities**.

That is a big simplification.

It also separates the problem into three very concrete sublemmas.

First, the coefficient \(A_j\) is the pure amplitude-cancellation quadratic term. It is the coefficient of \(\nu^2\), so it is detected by the slice
\[
\delta=0.
\]
Thus \(A_j=0\) would follow from a collision statement saying that on exact coincidence \(h_1=h_2\), the corrected defect vanishes to order \(>2\) in the amplitude-cancellation variable, or more strongly vanishes identically there. So the \(A_j\)-part is a pure **coincident-atom collision functoriality** question.

Second, the coefficient \(C_j\) is the pure separation term. It is detected by the slice
\[
\nu=0,
\]
that is, \(\lambda=1\). So \(C_3=c'\) and \(C_5=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'\) are exactly the **pure separation first-variation identities**. Those are the easiest-looking part of the target: they say the edge coefficient along zero amplitude-tilt is just the \(h\)-derivative of the one-pair witness.

Third, the coefficient \(B_j\) is the mixed term. It is the coefficient of \(\nu\delta\), so it is the only genuinely mixed infinitesimal interaction term. This is where the local amplitude ratio and the spatial separation first interact. Concretely,
\[
B_j(m)=\partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_j(m,0,0).
\]
So the whole local \(2\)-point problem is now compressed to a **mixed infinitesimal covariance identity**:
\[
B_3(m)=-\frac12 c(m),
\qquad
B_5(m)=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

This is, to my mind, the sharpest formulation yet.

Because once these six identities hold, the edge coefficients are exactly the model pair \((C,K)\), and then the local exclusion on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) is formal. Indeed, the model cubic edge
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m)
\]
has unique zero
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)},
\]
and at that slope
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa_*(m),0)
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
So on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), this is uniformly nonzero, and analytic perturbation in \(\delta^2\) excludes simultaneous vanishing of the actual cubic/quintic defects for sufficiently close cancelling configurations. This is exactly the stable local exclusion scheme we already had, but now reduced to six jet coefficients.

So the attack now yields a new theorem-level reduction:

> **Quadratic-jet reduction of the local \(2\)-point problem.**  
> On a compact good patch, local exclusion of close cancelling bad two-point cores follows from identifying the quadratic jet of the corrected cubic/quintic defects in the linearized swap chart \((\nu,\delta)\). Equivalently, it is enough to prove
> \[
> A_3=0,\quad B_3=-\frac12 c,\quad C_3=c',
> \]
> \[
> A_5=0,\quad B_5=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad C_5=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'.
> \]

This is much smaller than exact blown-up functoriality, smaller than full source-level merger, and sharper than the previous edge-value theorem.

It also clarifies what kinds of package-level input are still needed.

- \(A_j=0\) is a **coincident-atom collision functoriality** statement.
- \(C_j\) is a **pure separation first-variation** statement.
- \(B_j\) is the genuinely new **mixed infinitesimal covariance** statement.

So the next best attack is probably not another global structural theorem. It is to attack the mixed jet identities
\[
\partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_3(m,0,0)=-\frac12 c(m),
\qquad
\partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_5(m,0,0)=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
because those are now the only nontrivial coefficients not already suggested by the one-pair geometry.

That is the sharpest local normal form I can currently defend.

I can push the local attack one more step, and it sharpens the target into a very concrete **jet-matching problem**.

The last step reduced the good-patch local theorem to the quadratic coefficients of the corrected cubic/quintic defects in the linearized swap chart
\[
\nu:=\log\lambda,\qquad \delta:=h_2-h_1,
\]
where the atom-swap involution is exactly
\[
(\nu,\delta)\longmapsto(-\nu,-\delta).
\]
So for \(j=3,5\),
\[
E_j(m,\nu,\delta)
=
A_j(m)\nu^2+B_j(m)\nu\delta+C_j(m)\delta^2
+

\]
Equivalently, on the blown-up slope \(\nu=\kappa\delta+O(\delta^3)\),
\[
E_j=\delta^2\Bigl(A_j\kappa^2+B_j\kappa+C_j\Bigr)+O(\delta^4),
\]
so
\[
\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0)=A_j(m)\kappa^2+B_j(m)\kappa+C_j(m).
\]

The model pair coming from the one-pair directional law is
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\qquad
K(m,\kappa)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
so the desired identities are
\[
A_3=0,\qquad B_3=-\frac12 c,\qquad C_3=c',
\]
\[
A_5=0,\qquad B_5=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f},\qquad C_5=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'.
\]

What I think is new is that these six identities are **not equally hard**. They split into three qualitatively different slices.

First, \(C_j\) is the pure separation coefficient. It is read off from the slice
\[
\nu=0 \quad (\lambda=1),
\]
so it is a one-parameter first-variation problem:
\[
C_j(m)=\frac12\,\partial_\delta^2 E_j(m,0,0).
\]
This is the easiest-looking piece, because on \(\lambda=1\) you are only separating two equal-and-opposite atoms. If the corrected witness is differentiable in the separation parameter in the natural way, then \(C_3=c'\) and \(C_5=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'\) are exactly the expected first variations of the one-pair cubic/quintic data. So the \(C_j\)-identities should come from a **pure separation derivative theorem**.

Second, \(A_j\) is the pure amplitude-cancellation coefficient. It is read off from the slice
\[
\delta=0,
\]
so
\[
A_j(m)=\frac12\,\partial_\nu^2 E_j(m,0,0).
\]
This is a pure collision statement: how the corrected two-pair defect behaves when the two atoms coincide and only the cancellation ratio varies. So \(A_j=0\) is exactly the weakest collision-functoriality statement one could ask for at quadratic order. It does **not** require full merger, just that there is no pure-amplitude quadratic defect at exact coincidence. So the \(A_j\)-identities reduce to a **quadratic collision-sterility theorem**.

Third, \(B_j\) is the mixed coefficient:
\[
B_j(m)=\partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_j(m,0,0).
\]
This is the only genuinely mixed infinitesimal term. It measures how amplitude tilt and spatial separation couple at first nontrivial order. So the whole local \(2\)-point problem on a good patch has now been compressed to a **mixed infinitesimal covariance identity**
\[
\partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_3(m,0,0)=-\frac12 c(m),
\qquad
\partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_5(m,0,0)=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
That is the only part that still looks genuinely two-atom rather than inherited from one-pair geometry.

So the best current reduction is:

> **Quadratic-jet decomposition of the local problem.**  
> Local exclusion of close cancelling bad two-point cores on
> \[
> J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
> \]
> follows from three subtheorems:
> 1. pure separation first-variation:
>    \[
>    C_3=c',\qquad C_5=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})';
>    \]
> 2. pure amplitude-cancellation sterility:
>    \[
>    A_3=0,\qquad A_5=0;
>    \]
> 3. mixed infinitesimal covariance:
>    \[
>    B_3=-\frac12 c,\qquad B_5=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
>    \]

Once those hold, the model cubic coefficient
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m)
\]
has unique zero
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)},
\]
and then
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa_*(m),0)
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
So on any compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
this is uniformly nonzero, and analytic perturbation excludes simultaneous vanishing of the actual cubic/quintic defects for sufficiently small \(|\delta|\). That is the stable local exclusion theorem we already had, but now reduced to six explicit jet coefficients.

I think I can push one step further still: the \(A_j\)- and \(C_j\)-blocks are probably not the real obstruction anymore.

- \(C_j\) is one-pair differentiation along the pure separation slice. That should be derivable from ordinary smooth dependence of the corrected witness on \(h\).
- \(A_j\) is exact coincidence with pure amplitude cancellation. If there is any weak collision functoriality at all, this term should vanish.

So the only really new theorem likely left is the **mixed covariance block**:
\[
B_3=-\frac12 c,\qquad B_5=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

That suggests the next attack should be to isolate \(B_j\) directly from a two-parameter expansion along the mixed infinitesimal family
\[
(h_1,h_2,\lambda)
=
\left(m-\frac{\delta}{2},\,m+\frac{\delta}{2},\,e^\nu\right)
\]
and differentiate once in \(\delta\), once in \(\nu\), at \((\nu,\delta)=(0,0)\). If the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses are genuinely functorial to first order in the cancellation direction, those two mixed derivatives should be forced to the one-pair values above.

So my current best next theorem target is:

> **Mixed infinitesimal covariance theorem.**  
> In the linearized swap chart \((\nu,\delta)\), the corrected cubic/quintic defects satisfy
> \[
> \partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_3(m,0,0)=-\frac12 c(m),
> \qquad
> \partial_\nu\partial_\delta E_5(m,0,0)=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
> \]

If that lands, and if we can separately get the easier pure-slice identities for \(A_j\) and \(C_j\), then the local good-patch \(2\)-point exclusion is done.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 19:52:44)

_Thought for 22s_

I think the right next push is to **replace the mixed covariance theorem by a single directional first-variation theorem**. That is cleaner, and it shows that the mixed coefficient \(B_j\) is not really separate data.

We already reduced the corrected cubic/quintic defects to the quadratic-jet form in the linearized swap chart
\[
\nu:=\log\lambda,\qquad \delta:=h_2-h_1,
\]
where swap is exactly
\[
(\nu,\delta)\mapsto(-\nu,-\delta).
\]
So for \(j=3,5\),
\[
E_j(m,\nu,\delta)
=
A_j(m)\nu^2+B_j(m)\nu\delta+C_j(m)\delta^2
+
O\!\bigl((|\nu|+|\delta|)^4\bigr).
\]
Equivalently, along a slope \(\nu=\kappa\delta+O(\delta^3)\),
\[
E_j
=
\delta^2\Bigl(A_j(m)\kappa^2+B_j(m)\kappa+C_j(m)\Bigr)
+
O(\delta^4),
\]
so
\[
\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0)=A_j(m)\kappa^2+B_j(m)\kappa+C_j(m).
\]

The model pair we want is
\[
C(m,\kappa)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\qquad
K(m,\kappa)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]
That corresponds to
\[
A_3=0,\quad B_3=-\frac12 c,\quad C_3=c',
\]
\[
A_5=0,\quad B_5=-\frac12 A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad C_5=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'.
\]

The new point is: these six identities are equivalent to just **two** identities, one for each witness, namely
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
}
\]
for all \(\kappa\) near the relevant range.

So the clean theorem to attack is not the mixed covariance theorem alone. It is the **directional first-variation theorem at the cancellation edge**.

Why this is better is that the mixed coefficient \(B_j\) is then forced automatically: it is just the coefficient of \(\kappa\) in the directional law. In other words, \(B_j\) is not an independent mystery once the whole \(\kappa\)-dependence is identified.

Here is the geometric reason this directional law is the right one.

Take the local one-pair witness \(W_j(h)\), where
\[
W_3(h)=c(h),\qquad W_5(h)=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]
In the cancellation chart,
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad
\lambda=e^\nu=1+\nu+O(\nu^2).
\]
So the first-order cancelling source variation is
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\nu\,D_m-\delta\,D_m'+O\!\bigl((|\nu|+|\delta|)^2\bigr).
\]
Along a blow-up slope \(\nu=\kappa\delta\), that becomes
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\delta\Bigl(\frac{\kappa}{1}\,D_m+D_m'\Bigr)+O(\delta^2).
\]
Depending on normalization convention, this is exactly the affine cancellation direction behind the model operator
\[
V_\kappa:=\partial_h-\frac{\kappa}{2}\,\mathrm{Id}.
\]
So the proposed edge coefficient
\[
\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0)
\]
is precisely the first directional derivative of the one-pair witness \(W_j\) in the cancelling direction:
\[
\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0)=V_\kappa W_j(m).
\]
That is the conceptual theorem.

Once you write it that way, the earlier three-block decomposition becomes much clearer.

The pure separation coefficient \(C_j\) is just the \(\kappa=0\) value:
\[
C_j(m)=\mathcal H_j(m,0,0)=W_j'(m).
\]
So that part is ordinary one-pair differentiation.

The mixed coefficient \(B_j\) is just minus one-half the zeroth-order witness:
\[
B_j(m)=\partial_\kappa\mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0)\big|_{\kappa=0}
=-\frac12 W_j(m).
\]
So \(B_j\) is the infinitesimal amplitude-tilt response of the directional derivative law.

And the pure amplitude coefficient \(A_j\) vanishes because the directional law is affine, not quadratic, in \(\kappa\):
\[
A_j(m)=0.
\]

So the whole quadratic-jet target has now collapsed to:

> **Directional first-variation theorem at the cancellation edge.**  
> For the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses,
> \[
> \mathcal H_j(m,\kappa,0)=V_\kappa W_j(m),
> \qquad
> V_\kappa=\partial_h-\frac{\kappa}{2}\,\mathrm{Id},
> \]
> with \(W_3=c\) and \(W_5=A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

If that theorem holds, then all six jet identities follow at once, and the stable local exclusion on any compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
is formal.

Indeed, for \(j=3\),
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m)
\]
has unique zero
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
Then for \(j=5\),
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa_*(m),0)
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)}.
\]
So on \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), this is uniformly nonzero, and analytic perturbation in \(\delta^2\) excludes simultaneous vanishing of the actual cubic/quintic defects for sufficiently close cancelling configurations.

So the attack is now even cleaner than before:

- not six scalar identities,
- not even the mixed covariance theorem alone,
- but one directional edge theorem for \(c\) and one for \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

That is the sharpest local theorem target I can currently defend.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 19:53:38)

I’m pushing on the last reduction now: whether the directional edge theorem can be made formal from a minimal local-datum functoriality assumption, instead of needing full package functoriality.

_Thought for 27s_

I think the attack now reduces to a very small and very natural theorem, and it makes the directional first-variation law look almost inevitable.

The right move is to stop thinking of the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses as functions of the atom parameters \((h_1,h_2,\lambda)\), and instead think of them as functions of the **local cancellation datum**.

Write the relevant one-pair local datum at \(h\) as
\[
D_h.
\]
You can think of \(D_h\) as whichever local source germ or corrected block input the witness actually sees. The only properties we need are that \(h\mapsto D_h\) is analytic and that the one-pair cubic/quintic witnesses are analytic functionals of \(D_h\):
\[
W_3(D_h)=c(h),\qquad W_5(D_h)=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

Now pass to the collision-cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda=e^\nu,
\]
so swap is exactly
\[
(\nu,\delta)\mapsto(-\nu,-\delta).
\]
Then the two-atom cancellation datum expands as
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\delta\Bigl(D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m\Bigr)+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa:=\frac{\nu}{\delta},
\]
up to the harmless normalization convention on \(\kappa\). This is just the first-order cancellation direction in the blown-up chart.

So the natural infinitesimal direction is
\[
\Xi_\kappa(m):=D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m.
\]

Now here is the minimal theorem that would force everything we want:

> **Minimal local-datum edge functoriality.**  
> The quadratic edge coefficients of the corrected cubic/quintic defects depend only on the first-order cancellation direction \(\Xi_\kappa(m)\), through the same linear functionals that produce the one-pair witnesses.

In formulas, this says there are linear functionals \(L_3,L_5\) on first-order datum variations such that
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=L_3(\Xi_\kappa(m)),
\qquad
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=L_5(\Xi_\kappa(m)),
\]
and
\[
L_3(D_h)=c(h),\qquad L_5(D_h)=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

Once you write it that way, the desired edge law is formal. Because linearity gives
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)
=
L_3(D_m')+\frac{\kappa}{2}L_3(D_m),
\]
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)
=
L_5(D_m')+\frac{\kappa}{2}L_5(D_m).
\]
Up to the sign convention in the cancellation expansion, this is exactly
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\]
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

So the directional first-variation theorem is not really six scalar identities, nor even two separate formulas. It is just:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the edge coefficient is the linear response of the one-pair witness to the first-order cancellation datum.}
}
\]

That is the cleanest formulation so far.

It also explains why the coefficient split looked the way it did. In the quadratic-jet expansion
\[
E_j(m,\nu,\delta)
=
A_j(m)\nu^2+B_j(m)\nu\delta+C_j(m)\delta^2+O((|\nu|+|\delta|)^4),
\]
the pure separation term \(C_j\) comes from the \(D_m'\) part of \(\Xi_\kappa\), the mixed term \(B_j\) comes from the \(D_m\) part, and the pure amplitude term \(A_j\) vanishes because \(\Xi_\kappa\) is affine in \(\kappa\), not quadratic. So the earlier decomposition into \(A\), \(B\), and \(C\) was really a shadow of one linear directional law.

This gives a much better theorem target:

> **Cancellation-edge linear response theorem.**  
> The corrected cubic/quintic edge coefficients are obtained by applying the one-pair witness functionals to the first-order cancellation direction
> \[
> \Xi_\kappa(m)=D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m,
> \]
> with the appropriate sign convention.

If that theorem holds, then on a compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
local exclusion is formal. Indeed,
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m)
\]
has unique zero
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)},
\]
and then
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa_*(m),0)
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
=
\frac{M(m)}{c(m)},
\]
which is uniformly nonzero on \(J\). Analytic perturbation in \(\delta^2\) then excludes simultaneous vanishing of the actual cubic/quintic defects for sufficiently close cancelling configurations.

So the math attack has now reduced the local good-patch \(2\)-point theorem to one minimal package-level statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{edge quadratic coefficients }=\text{ linear response of the one-pair witnesses to the cancellation direction.}
}
\]

That is smaller than exact blown-up functoriality, smaller than full source-level merger, and conceptually cleaner than the earlier mixed-covariance formulation.

The only real remaining question is whether the actual corrected package is functorial enough at first order in the cancellation datum for this linear response theorem to be true. That is, to my mind, the sharpest local theorem still standing.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 19:55:11)

_Thought for 7s_

I can push it one more step, and I think this isolates the exact infinitesimal statement that would finish the good-patch local theorem.

The cancellation-edge linear response theorem can be weakened further. It does not need full functoriality of the corrected package in arbitrary local data. It only needs **first-order homogeneity and directional differentiability at the zero datum**.

Here is the clean setup.

Let \(D_h\) denote the local one-pair datum seen by the corrected witness, and let
\[
W_3(D_h)=c(h),\qquad W_5(D_h)=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]
In the cancellation chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda=e^\nu,
\]
the two-atom cancellation datum has first-order expansion
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
-\delta\Bigl(D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m\Bigr)+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{\nu}{\delta},
\]
up to the fixed sign convention. So the relevant tangent direction is
\[
\Xi_\kappa(m):=D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m.
\]

Now suppose the corrected cubic/quintic defects arise from analytic functionals
\[
\mathcal F_3,\mathcal F_5
\]
of the local cancellation datum, with
\[
\mathcal F_j(0)=0,
\]
and such that the first nonzero term at the zero datum is quadratic in the atom variables but only **first-order in the cancellation datum**. Then the edge coefficients are simply the directional derivatives of \(\mathcal F_j\) at \(0\) evaluated on \(\Xi_\kappa(m)\):
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=d\mathcal F_3|_{0}\bigl(\Xi_\kappa(m)\bigr),
\qquad
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=d\mathcal F_5|_{0}\bigl(\Xi_\kappa(m)\bigr).
\]

So the local theorem reduces to identifying these two linear maps:
\[
d\mathcal F_3|_{0}=L_3,\qquad d\mathcal F_5|_{0}=L_5,
\]
with
\[
L_3(D_h)=c(h),\qquad L_5(D_h)=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h).
\]

If that holds, then immediately
\[
\mathcal H_3(m,\kappa,0)=L_3\!\left(D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m\right)
=
c'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}c(m),
\]
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa,0)=L_5\!\left(D_m'+\frac{\kappa}{2}D_m\right)
=
(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m)-\frac{\kappa}{2}A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
again up to the global sign convention already fixed in the chart.

That is enough for the whole local exclusion scheme on
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\qquad
M=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c' A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Indeed, the cubic edge coefficient has unique zero
\[
\kappa_*(m)=2\frac{c'(m)}{c(m)},
\]
and then
\[
\mathcal H_5(m,\kappa_*(m),0)=\frac{M(m)}{c(m)},
\]
which is uniformly nonzero on \(J\). Analytic perturbation in \(\delta^2\) then excludes simultaneous vanishing of the actual cubic/quintic defects for sufficiently close cancelling configurations.  

So the attack has reduced the local good-patch theorem to an even smaller statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the quadratic edge coefficients are the Fréchet derivatives at zero of the corrected defect functionals.}
}
\]

That means the real remaining local obstruction is no longer “mysterious two-atom geometry.” It is whether the corrected package has the expected **tangent map at the zero cancellation datum**.

This also clarifies the role of the earlier jet coefficients \(A_j,B_j,C_j\). They are not independent data anymore. They are just the coordinates of the single linear functional \(d\mathcal F_j|_0\) on the two-dimensional tangent space spanned by
\[
D_m,\qquad D_m'.
\]
Concretely:

- \(A_j=0\) says the edge law is linear, not quadratic, in the cancellation direction.
- \(B_j\) and \(C_j\) are just the components of the same linear map on \(D_m\) and \(D_m'\).

So the whole six-coefficient problem has collapsed to identifying two tangent maps.

That gives the sharpest local theorem target I can currently defend:

> **Zero-datum tangent-map theorem.**  
> For the corrected cubic/quintic defect functionals, the differential at the zero cancellation datum coincides with the one-pair cubic/quintic witness maps.

If that theorem holds, the local \(2\)-point exclusion on compact good patches is done.

The only way the local theorem can still fail after this reduction is if the actual corrected package is **not differentiable in the needed sense at the zero cancellation datum**, or if its tangent map is not the one-pair witness map. That is a much narrower and cleaner obstruction than anything we had earlier.
